Intention for Udhiyah: Timing and Designation
Rule on intention timing and its branches

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that intention for udhiyah is required at purchase, not slaughter, and identify the consequences in subsidiary cases including unauthorized slaughter and designation.

Core Idea
Intention for udhiyah must be at purchase; the animal becomes absolutely designated and cannot be sold even by the rich.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir presents a key rule (qa'ida) regarding udhiyah: the intention (niyyah) must be made at the time of purchase, not at slaughter. The author then expands on this rule by deriving subsidiary rulings (furu'at) covering scenarios where someone else slaughters the animal without permission, and whether the animal becomes specifically designated for the sacrifice. Understanding these branches is essential for a mufti when advising on sacrificial practices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Base Rule
Locate the main legal principle stated at the beginning: 'As for sacrifices, intention is necessary, but at the time of purchase, not at slaughter.' This is the qa'ida.
The rule is precise: intention at purchase, not slaughter.
2
Trace the First Furu'
The author says 'A subsidiary ruling derived from this is: If one buys with intention and someone else slaughters without permission...' Note the two outcomes: if owner takes it without demanding compensation, it suffices; if he demands compensation, it does not.
This highlights the role of intention and acceptance.
3
Analyze the Designation (Ta'ayyun) Issue
The passage then asks whether the animal becomes designated by intention. Two views: one based on wealth (poor/rich), then the correct view (sahih) that it is absolute. Understand the legal effect: even a rich person must give the animal away alive after Eid, but can substitute another.
The correct view simplifies the rule.
4
Apply the Analogy to Hadi
The final sentence extends the same ruling to hadi (sacrificial animals for Hajj): 'Hadi are like udhiyah.'
This is a qiyas extension.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الضحايا فلا بد فيها من النيَّة، لكن عند الشراء لا عند الذبح وتفرّع عليه أنه لو اشتراها بنية الأضحية فذبحها غيره بلا إذن فإن أخذها مذبوحة ولم يضمنه أجزأته، وإن ضمنه لا يجزىء كما في أُضحية الذخيرة، وهذا إذا ذبحها عن نفسه، أما إذا ذبحها عن مالكها فلا ضمان عليه وهل تتعيَّن الأضحية بالنيَّة؟ قالوا: إن كان فقيرا وقد اشتراها بنيتها تعينت فليس له بيعها، وإن كان غنيا لم تتعيَّن والصحيح أنها تتعين مطلقا فيتصدق بها الغني بعد أيامها حيَّة ولكن له أن يقيم غيرها مقامها، كما في البدائع من الأضحية قالوا والهدايا كالضحايا
As for sacrifices (udhiyah), intention is necessary, but at the time of purchase, not at slaughter. A subsidiary ruling derived from this is: If one buys an animal with the intention of udhiyah, and someone else slaughters it without permission, then if the owner takes it slaughtered and does not hold the slaughterer liable (i.e., does not demand compensation), it suffices; if he holds him liable (demands compensation), it does not suffice, as in Udhiyah of al-Dhakhirah. This is if he slaughters it for himself; but if he slaughters it for its owner, there is no liability. Does the udhiyah become designated (ta'ayyun) by intention? They said: If the owner is poor and bought it with the intention, it becomes designated, so he cannot sell it. If he is rich, it does not become designated. The correct view is that it becomes designated absolutely; even the rich person must give it away alive after the days of tashriq, but he can replace it with another. As in al-Bada'i' on udhiyah. They said: Hadi (sacrificial animals for Hajj) are like udhiyah.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage addresses the role of intention in udhiyah (the sacrifice on Eid al-Adha). The intention must be made at the time of purchase, not at slaughter. A furu' (branch ruling) is given: if someone buys an animal with the intention of udhiyah, and another person slaughters it without permission, the outcome depends on whether the owner demands compensation. If he accepts the meat and does not seek payment, the sacrifice is valid; if he demands compensation, it is not valid because his claim indicates he did not accept the intended sacrifice. If the unauthorized slaughterer slaughters it for the owner (i.e., as a gift), there is no liability. The passage then discusses whether the animal becomes specifically designated (ta'ayyun) for udhiyah by intention. According to one view, if the owner is poor, it becomes designated; if rich, not. The correct view (sahih) is that it becomes designated absolutely, so even a rich person must give the animal away alive after Eid, but he can substitute another animal for the sacrifice. Hadi (sacrificial animals during Hajj) follows the same rules.

Key Terms
الضحايا (al-dahaya): Sacrificial animals offered on Eid al-Adha.
تتعين (tata'ayyan): Becomes designated or specified; once designated, the animal cannot be sold or replaced.
النية (al-niyyah): Intention; a condition for the validity of the sacrifice, must be made at purchase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view (sahih) in this passage, what happens if a rich person buys an animal with intention of udhiyah?
A) He can sell it because he is rich.
B) It becomes designated absolutely; he cannot sell it.
C) It does not become designated; he may sell it.
D) He must slaughter it himself.

Key Takeaway
The intention for udhiyah must be made at the time of purchase, not at slaughter, and the animal becomes absolutely designated upon that intention, with subsidiary rulings flowing from this core rule.

Niyyah in Manumission (Itq)
Rule on intention in manumission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule distinguishing sarih and kinayah in manumission to determine validity, reward, and potential sin.

Core Idea
Explicit manumission needs no intention; implicit does.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair explains a key distinction in Hanafi law regarding the role of intention (niyyah) in manumission. Understanding this rule is crucial for anyone issuing fatwas on the validity of freeing slaves, as it separates the requirements for legal effect from those for reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine that manumission (itq) is the act under discussion. Note that it is not inherently an act of worship because it is valid from a disbeliever. Identify the hukm: it can be valid without intention if sarih.
Focus on the nature of itq as a worldly contract, not devotional.
2
Distinguish sarih from kinayah
Differentiate between explicit wording (sarih, e.g., 'you are free') and implicit wording (kinayah, e.g., 'leave'). Note that sarih is valid without intention, while kinayah requires intention for validity.
Sarih does not need niyyah; kinayah does.
3
Analyze cases of incorrect intention
Consider scenarios where the intention is for an idol, Satan, or a created being. Understand the rulings: for a disbeliever freeing for an idol, it is valid but sinful; for a Muslim doing so with veneration, it is kufr. Freeing for a created being is valid but disliked (makruh).
Intention affects sinfulness but not validity in sarih.
4
Extend the rule to tadbir and kitabah
Recognize that the same rules apply to tadbir (freeing after death) and kitabah (contract for freedom) as to immediate manumission.
Tadbir and kitabah follow the same principles.
5
Formulate the fatwa hierarchy
Summarize the operative rulings: for sarih, intention not required for validity but needed for reward; for kinayah, intention is required for validity. The mufta bihi is as stated in the passage.
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما العتق فعندنا ليس بعبادة وضعا بدليل صحته من الكافر ولا عبادة له، فإن نوى وجه الله كان عبادة مُثابًا عليها، وإن أعتق بلا نيَّة صح، ولا ثواب له إن كان صريحًا. وأما الكناية، فلا بد لها من النيَّة، وإن أعتق للصنم أو للشيطان صح وأيم، وإن أعتق لأجل مخلوق صح وكان مُباحًا لا ثواب ولا إثم وينبغي أن يخصص بالإعتاق للصنم بما إذا كان المعتق كافرًا، أما المسلم إذا أعتق له قاصدًا تعظيمه كفر، كما ينبغي أن يكون الإعتاق لمخلوق مكروها والتدبير والكتابة كالعتق
As for manumission (itq), according to us (Hanafis), it is not a devotional act by nature (wad'an), as evidenced by its validity when performed by a disbeliever, and he has no act of worship. If one intends the countenance of Allah, it becomes worship with reward. If one frees a slave without intention, it is valid, but there is no reward if it was explicit (sarih). As for implicit (kinayah) manumission, intention is necessary. If one frees [a slave] for an idol or for Satan, it is valid and [sinful?]. If one frees for the sake of a created being, it is valid and permissible, with no reward or sin. It should be specified that freeing for an idol is applicable when the emancipator is a disbeliever; if a Muslim frees for the purpose of venerating it, it is disbelief. Similarly, freeing for a created being is disliked (makruh). Tadbir (freeing after death) and kitabah (contract for freedom) are like manumission.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage discusses the role of intention in manumission (itq). According to Hanafis, manumission is not inherently an act of worship (ibadah) because it is valid even from a disbeliever, and a disbeliever's actions are not worship. However, if done with sincere intention for Allah, it becomes a rewarded act. For explicit manumission (clear words like 'you are free'), intention is not required for validity but is needed for reward. For implicit (kinayah, e.g., 'leave'), intention is required for the act to be effective. If one frees a slave for the sake of an idol or Satan, the emancipation is valid but sinful. However, this applies only to a disbeliever; a Muslim doing so with veneration commits kufr. Freeing for the sake of a created being (e.g., to please someone) is valid but disliked (makruh). Tadbir (the master's declaration that the slave will be free after his death) and kitabah (a contract where the slave buys his freedom) follow the same rules as manumission.

Key Terms
الصريح (al-sarih): Explicit, unambiguous wording for manumission, e.g., 'you are free'.
الكناية (al-kinayah): Implicit wording that can imply manumission but is not direct.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Muslim explicitly says 'you are free' to his slave without any intention, is the manumission valid?
A) No, intention is required.
B) Yes, it is valid but without reward.
C) Yes, it is valid and rewarded.
D) It depends on the owner's wealth.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, explicit manumission does not require intention for validity; implicit does; intention affects reward and sin.

Intention in Marriage: Reward vs. Validity
Rule: intention in marriage is for reward, not validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that intention in marriage is for reward, not validity, and identify the mufta bihi position regarding contracts with deficient intention or wording.

Core Idea
Marriage is valid without sincere intention; intention only affects reward.

In Hanafi fiqh, marriage (nikah) is considered close to worship, and engaging in it with proper intention earns great reward. However, the school makes a sharp distinction between validity (sihhah) and reward (thawab). This passage from Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir clarifies that intention is not a condition for the validity of marriage, and even if the contract is made jokingly or with words not understood, it remains valid according to the relied-upon position. This ruling is a key principle for muftis when advising on marriage issues.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule regarding intention and validity
Understand that the passage explicitly states intention is not a condition for validity (shart sihhah). Instead, it is required for reward.
Contrast this with other contracts where intention may affect validity.
2
Analyze the exception: marriage jokingly (hazl)
Note that even if the marriage contract is made in jest, it is still valid. This is a unique feature of nikah, as many contracts are invalidated by hazl.
Hazl means joking without serious intent.
3
Examine the disputed case: unknown words
If the contract is made with words whose meaning is not known by the parties, there is a difference of opinion. The fatwa (mufta bihi) is that it is still valid, regardless of witnesses' knowledge.
This shows the strength of the validity of nikah.
4
Apply the rule to a fatwa scenario
As a mufti, when asked about a marriage where the couple did not understand the Arabic wording or acted jokingly, you should rule that the marriage is valid, but advise them to renew their intention for reward.
The mufti should also note the importance of educating the parties about the meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما النكاح فقالوا إنه أقرب إلى العبادات حتى أن الاشتغال به أفضل من التخلي لمحض العبادة. وهو عند الاعتدال سُنّة مؤكدة على الصحيح فيحتاج إلى النية لتحصيل الثواب ؛ وهو أن يقصد إعفاف نفسه وتحصينها وحصول ولد. وفسرنا الاعتدال في الشرح الكبير شرح الكنز، ولم تكن فيه شرط صحة قالوا يصح النكاح مع الهزل، لكن قالوا حتى لو عقد بلفظ لا يعرف معناه ففيه خلاف والفتوى على صحته، علم الشهود أو لا كما في البزازية.
As for marriage (nikah), they said it is closest to acts of worship such that engaging in it is better than secluding oneself for pure worship. When [done] in moderation, it is a confirmed sunnah according to the correct view. Therefore, it requires intention to obtain reward: one should intend to protect himself and his spouse from sin and to have children. We have explained moderation in al-Sharh al-Kabir (commentary on al-Kanz). Intention is not a condition for validity; they (the scholars) said that marriage is valid even if done jokingly. However, they said even if the contract is made with words whose meaning is not known, there is disagreement, but the fatwa is on its validity, whether the witnesses know the meaning or not, as in al-Bazzaziyyah.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage discusses the role of intention in marriage (nikah). Marriage is considered close to acts of worship; it is a confirmed sunnah when done in moderation, and engaging in it is better than abandoning it for constant worship. Intention is necessary for reward: one should intend to safeguard himself from illicit relations, protect his spouse, and have children. However, intention is not a condition for the validity (sihhah) of the marriage contract. Even if the contract is made jokingly (hazl), it is valid. Furthermore, if the contract is made with words that the parties do not understand, there is a difference of opinion, but the fatwa (relied-upon position) is that it is still valid, regardless of whether the witnesses understand the meaning or not, as stated in al-Bazzaziyyah. This underscores that the formal validity of marriage does not depend on the presence of intention or comprehension of the words, but reward is tied to sincere intention.

Key Terms
الهزل (al-hazl): Joking; entering into a contract without serious intent.
النية (al-niyyah): Intention; the purpose behind an act.
شرط الصحة (shart al-sihhah): Condition for validity; something required for the act to be legally sound.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, is a marriage contract valid if it is made jokingly?
A) No, it is void.
B) Yes, it is valid.
C) Only if the witnesses are aware of the joke.
D) Only if the intention is for reward.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, marriage is valid without sincere intention or even understanding of the words; intention only affects reward.

Intention in Acts of Worship and Permissible Acts
Expansion of intention requirement across acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that intention is required for reward in acts of worship and permissible acts, and identify which acts require intention for validity.

Core Idea
Intention earns reward; without it, the act may still be valid but unrewarded.

The great maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' governs many aspects of fiqh. This passage from al-Ashbah wal-Naza'ir applies it to a range of acts—some obviously devotional, others seemingly mundane. Understanding where intention affects reward versus validity is crucial for both worship and worldly dealings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
For each act mentioned (jihad, wasiyyah, waqf, qada', hudud, ta'azir, shahadat, mubahat), note whether it is an act of worship (ibadah) or a permissible act (mubah).
Jihad and qada' are considered from the greatest acts of worship; waqf is not worship by nature.
2
Distinguish reward vs. validity
For each act, determine whether intention (niyyah) is a condition for reward (thawab) or for the validity (sihhah) of the act. The text explicitly states that wasiyyah is valid even without intention, but reward depends on it.
The ruling for jihad implies intention is necessary; likely for both reward and validity given its nature.
3
Apply to permissible acts (mubahat)
Permissible acts like eating, sleeping, earning, and marital relations become acts of worship if intended to aid in fulfilling obligations. The change in ruling depends on intention.
This is a classic application of the maxim: the act itself is neutral; intention transforms it.
4
Extract the underlying qawida
From these examples, derive the sub-maxim: 'Intention is required for reward in acts that can be directed toward Allah; it is not required for validity in worldly acts unless specified otherwise.'
This is a branch of the greater qawida 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الجهاد، فمن أعظم العبادات، فلا بد من خلوص النيَّة. وأم الوصية فكالعتق إن قصد التقرب فله الثواب وإلا فهي صحيحة فقط. وأما الوقف فليس عبادة وضعًا بدليل صحته من الكافر فإن نوى القربة فله الثواب، وإلا فلا. وأما النكاح فقالوا إنه أقرب إلى العبادات حتى أن الاشتغال به أفضل من التخلي لمحض العبادة. وهو عند الاعتدال سُنّة مؤكدة على الصحيح فيحتاج إلى النية لتحصيل الثواب؛ وهو أن يقصد إعفاف نفسه وتحصينها وحصول ولد. وفسرنا الاعتدال في الشرح الكبير شرح الكنز، ولم تكن فيه شرط صحة قالوا يصح النكاح مع الهزل، لكن قالوا حتى لو عقد بلفظ لا يعرف معناه ففيه خلاف والفتوى على صحته، علم الشهود أو لا كما في البزازية. وعلى هذا سائر القرب لا بد فيها من النية، بمعنى توقف حصول الثواب على قصد التقرب بها إلى الله تعالى من نشر العلم تعليمًا وإفتاء وتصنيفا . وأما القضاء، فقالوا إنه من أشرف العبادات والثواب عليه، أي على القضاء، متوقف عليها، أي على النية، وكذا إقامة الحدود والتعازير، وكل ما يتعاطاه الحكام والولاة، وكذا الشهادات وأداؤها. وأما المُباحات فإنها تختلف صفتها باعتبار ما قصدت لأجله. فإذا قصد بها التقوي على الطاعات أو التوصل إليها كانت عبادة، كالأكل والنوم واكتساب المال والوطء . وأما المعاملات فأنواع فالبيع لا يتوقف عليها، وكذا الإقالة والإجارة، لكن قالوا إن عقد بمضارع لم يصدر بسوف أو السين توقف على النيَّة، فإن نوى به
As for jihad, it is among the greatest acts of worship, so purity of intention is necessary. As for the will (wasiyyah), it is like manumission: if one intends to draw near to Allah, he gets reward; otherwise, it is merely valid. As for endowment (waqf), it is not worship by nature, as evidenced by its validity from a disbeliever; if one intends nearness, he gets reward; otherwise, no. As for judiciary (qada'), they said it is among the noblest acts of worship, and reward for it—i.e., for judging—is dependent on intention. Likewise, establishing hadd punishments and discretionary punishments (ta'azir), and everything that rulers and governors undertake, as well as testimonies and their performance. As for permissible acts (mubahat), their nature varies according to what they are intended for. If one intends by them to gain strength for obedience or to achieve it, they become worship, like eating, sleeping, earning wealth, and sexual intercourse. As for transactions (mu'amalat), their types: sale does not depend on intention, and likewise refund (iqalah) and lease (ijarah). But they said if a contract is made using the present tense verb (mudari') without the future particles 'sawfa' or 'sin', it is dependent on intention; if he intends by it [the present tense as actual contract], then it is valid.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage covers the role of intention in various acts: Jihad requires pure intention (ikhlas). A will (wasiyyah) follows the same rule as manumission: if done with the intention of drawing near to Allah, it is rewarded; otherwise, it is merely valid. Endowment (waqf) is not inherently an act of worship (since a disbeliever can do it), but with intention for Allah, it brings reward. The judiciary (qada') is considered one of the noblest forms of worship, and reward for judging is contingent on the judge's intention. Similarly, implementing hadd punishments and ta'azir, and all functions of rulers and governors, as well as giving testimony, require intention for reward. Permissible acts (mubahat) like eating, sleeping, earning, and marital relations become worship if intended to aid in fulfilling obligations. For transactions (mu'amalat), sale, iqalah (cancellation of sale), and ijarah (lease) do not require intention for validity. However, if a contract is expressed using the present tense verb (e.g., 'I sell') without future particles like 'sawfa' or 'sin', the validity depends on the intention of the speaker—whether he actually means to create the contract. This is because the present tense can also indicate future intent.

Key Terms
النية (al-niyyah): Intention, the mental resolve to perform an act for Allah or for a specific purpose.
المباحات (al-mubahat): Permissible acts, which are neutral in ruling but can become rewarding through intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following acts, according to the passage, does NOT require intention for validity?
A) Jihad
B) Will (wasiyyah)
C) Judiciary (qada')
D) Permissible acts when directed to obedience

Key Takeaway
Intention is the key to reward; validity can stand without it in non-worship acts.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications

AL-UMUR BI-MAQASIDIHA: Intention Across Fiqh Chapters
Qa'ida with furu' across multiple chapters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to distinguish when intention is required for validity, when only for reward, and when not required, using examples from worship, transactions, family law, and oaths.

Core Idea
Intention determines reward but not always validity; explicit acts like divorce occur even without intention.

The Hanafi school is known for its nuanced treatment of intention (niyyah). While the maxim 'Matters are judged by their intentions' is universal, its application varies across chapters: some acts require intention for validity, others only for reward, and others not at all. This lesson walks through the major furu' (branches) to show you how the same qa'ida yields different rulings depending on the nature of the act and the wording used.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its nature
Is the act inherently a worship (ibadah) or a custom (muamalah)? Acts that are worship by nature (like salah, sawm) always require intention for validity. Acts that are not inherently worship (like emancipation, marriage) do not require intention for validity, but intention brings reward.
2
Determine the wording: explicit or implicit?
Explicit (sarih) wording directly indicates the legal effect without context. Implicit (kinayah) wording requires intention to specify the intended effect. For explicit acts, intention is often not needed for judicial validity.
e.g., 'you are divorced' is sarih; 'you are haram upon me' is kinayah.
3
Check if intention affects validity or only reward
For acts like sale, marriage, and explicit divorce, intention does not affect validity. For acts like implicit divorce or gifts with jest, intention may be needed or not depending on other factors like consent.
4
Note exceptions: jest and coercion
Jesting in divorce and emancipation still makes them effective (lest the law be trivialized). Coercion invalidates transactions but not divorce/emancipation. These exceptions are built into the maxim.
5
Apply the maxim to a new case
Given a scenario, classify the act, check wording, identify if intention is required for validity/reward, and state the ruling accordingly.

الثواب، وإلا فلا. وأما النكاح فقالوا إنه أقرب إلى العبادات حتى أن الاشتغال به أفضل من التخلي لمحض العبادة. وهو عند الاعتدال سُنّة مؤكدة على الصحيح فيحتاج إلى النية لتحصيل الثواب ؛ وهو أن يقصد إعفاف نفسه وتحصينها وحصول ولد. وفسرنا الاعتدال في الشرح الكبير شرح الكنز، ولم تكن فيه شرط صحة قالوا يصح النكاح مع الهزل، لكن قالوا حتى لو عقد بلفظ لا يعرف معناه ففيه خلاف والفتوى على صحته، علم الشهود أو لا كما في البزازية. وعلى هذا سائر القرب لا بد فيها من النية، بمعنى توقف حصول الثواب على قصد التقرب بها إلى الله تعالى من نشر العلم تعليمًا وإفتاء وتصنيفا . وأما القضاء، فقالوا إنه من أشرف العبادات والثواب عليه، أي على القضاء، متوقف عليها، أي على النية، وكذا إقامة الحدود والتعازير، وكل ما يتعاطاه الحكام والولاة، وكذا الشهادات وأداؤها. وأما المُباحات فإنها تختلف صفتها باعتبار ما قصدت لأجله. فإذا قصد بها التقوي على الطاعات أو التوصل إليها كانت عبادة، كالأكل والنوم واكتساب المال والوطء . وأما المعاملات فأنواع فالبيع لا يتوقف عليها، وكذا الإقالة والإجارة، لكن قالوا إن عقد بمضارع لم يصدر بسوف أو السين توقف على النيَّة، فإن نوى به الإيجاب للحال كان بيعًا، وإلا لا . بخلاف صيغة الماضي فإن البيع بها لا يتوقف على النيَّة، وأما المضارع المتمخض للاستقبال فهو كالأمر لا يصح البيع به ولا بالنية. وقد أوضحناه في شرح الكنز. وقالوا لا يصح مع الهزل لعدم الرضى بحكمه معه وأما الهبة فلا تتوقف على النيَّة. قالوا لو وهب مازحًا صحت، كما في البزازية، ولكن لو لقن الهبة ولم يعرفها لم تصح لا لأجل أن النية شرطها، وإنما هو لفقد شرطها وهو الرضى، ولذا لو أكره عليها لم تصح بخلاف الطلاق والعتاق؛ فإنهما يقعان بالتلقين ممن لا يعرفهما، لأن الرضى ليس بشرطهما. ولذا لو أكره عليهما يقعان . وأما الطلاق، فصريح وكناية. فالأول لا يحتاج في وقوعه إليها؛ فلو طلق غافلاً أو ساهيًا أو مخطئًا وقع حتى قالوا: إن الطلاق يقع بالألفاظ المصحفة قضاء، ولكن لا بد أن يقصدها باللفظ قالوا لو كرّر مسائل الطلاق بحضرتها ويقول في كل مرة : أنت طالق لم يقع الطلاق بحضرتها ولو كتبت امرأتي طالق أو أنت طالق، وقالت له اقرأ عليّ فقرأ عليها لم يقع لعدم قصده باللفظ ولا ينافيه قولهم إن الصريح لا يحتاج إلى النية . وقالوا : لو قال أنت طالق ناويًا الطلاق من وثاق لم يقع ديانة ووقع قضاء، وفي عبارة بعض الكتب أن طلاق المخطىء واقع قضاء لا ديانة، فظهر بهذا أن الصريح لا يحتاج إليها قضاء ويحتاج إليها ديانة ولا يردّ عليه قولهم إنه لو طلقها هازلاً يقع عليه قضاء وديانة، لأن الشارع جعل هزله به جدا. وقالوا لا تصح نية الثلاث في أنت طالق ولا نيَّة البائن، ولا تصح نيَّة الثنتين في المصدر؛ أنت الطلاق إلا أن تكون المرأة أمة وتصح نيَّة الثلاث وأما كناياته فلا يقع بها إلا بالنية ديانة، سواء كان معها مذاكرة الطلاق أو لا . والمذاكرة إنما تقوم مقام النية في القضاء إلا في لفظ الحرام، فإنه كناية ولا يحتاج إليها فينصرف إلى الطلاق إذا كان الزوج من قوم يريدون بالحرام الطلاق وأما تفويض الطلاق والخلع والإيلاء والظهار، فما كان منه صريحًا لا يشترط له النيَّة، وما كان كناية اشترطت له وأما الرجعة فكالنكاح لأنها استدامته، لكن ما كان منها صريحًا لا يحتاج إليها، وكنايتها تحتاج إليها . وأما اليمين بالله ؛ فلا تتوقف عليها، فينعقد إذا حلف عامدًا أو ساهيًا أو مخطئًا أو مكرها. وكذا إذا فعل المحلوف عليه كذلك. وأما نيَّة تخصيص العام في اليمين فمقبولة ديانة اتفاقا وقضاء عند الخصاف، والفتوى على قوله إن كان الحالف مظلومًا. وكذلك اختلفوا هل الاعتبار لنيَّة الحالف أو لنيَّة المستحلف؟ والفتوى على
It suffices, as in the udhiyah of al-Dhakhirah. This is if he slaughters for himself; but if he slaughters for its owner, there is no liability. Does the udhiyah become specific by intention? They said: If he is poor and bought it with its intention, it becomes specific so he cannot sell it; if he is rich, it does not become specific. The correct view is that it becomes specific absolutely, so the rich person gives it in charity alive after its days, but he can replace it. As in al-Bada'i' regarding udhiyah; they said gifts (hadiyya) are like udhiyah. As for emancipation (itq), according to us it is not a worship by nature, evidenced by its validity from a disbeliever who has no worship. If he intends the face of Allah, it becomes worship rewarded. If he emancipates without intention, it is valid but no reward if it is explicit. As for implicit (kinaya), intention is necessary. If he emancipates for an idol or for Satan, it is valid and [sinful?]. If he emancipates for a creature, it is valid and permissible, no reward or sin. It should be specified that emancipation for an idol is if the emancipator is a disbeliever; if a Muslim does it intending veneration, he becomes a disbeliever. Also, emancipation for a creature should be disliked. Tadbir and kitaba are like emancipation. As for jihad, it is one of the greatest acts of worship, so sincerity of intention is necessary. As for will (wasiyya), it is like emancipation: if he intends nearness, he gets reward; otherwise it is merely valid. As for endowment (waqf), it is not worship by nature, evidenced by its validity from a disbeliever; if he intends the act of devotion, he gets reward; otherwise not. As for marriage (nikah), they said it is closer to acts of worship so that engaging in it is better than seclusion for mere worship. In moderation it is confirmed sunnah according to the correct view, so intention is needed for reward: he intends to protect himself and have offspring. We explained moderation in al-Sharh al-Kabir Sharh al-Kanz. It is not a condition of validity. They said marriage is valid with jest, but if contracted with a word whose meaning is unknown, there is a difference of opinion and the fatwa is on its validity whether the witnesses know or not, as in al-Bazzaziyya. Similarly, all acts of devotion require intention in the sense that obtaining reward depends on intending nearness to Allah, including spreading knowledge, teaching, giving fatwa, and writing. As for judgment (qada'), they said it is one of the noblest worships, and reward for it depends on intention. Similarly, establishing hadd penalties and discretionary punishments, and all that judges and governors do, and testimony and its performance. As for permissible acts, their legal status varies according to what they are intended for: if intended for strength to obey or to reach obedience, they become worship, like eating, sleeping, earning wealth, and intercourse. As for transactions: sale does not depend on intention; similarly, rescission (iqala) and leasing; but they said if contracted in the present tense (mudari') that is not preceded by 'sawfa' or 'sin', intention is required: if he intends present obligation it is a sale, otherwise not. Contrast the past tense form; sale with it does not require intention. The present tense exclusively for future is like a command; sale is not valid with it nor with intention. We explained this in Sharh al-Kanz. They said sale is not valid with jest due to lack of consent. As for gift (hiba), it does not depend on intention; they said if one gives jokingly, it is valid, as in al-Bazzaziyya. But if he is taught (prompted) the gift and does not know it, it is not valid, not because intention is a condition, but due to lack of consent (rida). Hence if coerced, it is not valid, contrary to divorce and emancipation, which occur by prompting even if the person does not know them, because consent is not a condition; even if coerced, they occur. As for divorce (talaq), it is explicit (sarih) and implicit (kinaya). The former does not require intention for its occurrence; if he divorces forgetfully, carelessly, or mistakenly, it occurs. They said divorce occurs with mispronounced words in qada' (court), but he must intend the words. They said: if he repeatedly recites the issues of divorce in her presence and says each time 'you are divorced', divorce does not occur if written 'my wife is divorced' or 'you are divorced' and she says 'read to me' and he reads it, it does not occur for lack of intending the words. This does not contradict their statement that explicit does not need intention. And they said: if he says 'you are divorced' intending divorce from a shackle, it does not occur in dianah (conscience) but occurs in qada'. In some books it is said that the mistaken divorce occurs in qada' not dianah. Thus it appears that explicit does not need intention in qada' but needs it in dianah. This is not contradicted by their statement that if he divorces jokingly, it occurs in qada' and dianah, because the Lawgiver has made his jest serious. They said: intention of three is not valid in 'you are divorced' nor intention of ba'in (irrevocable), nor intention of two in the masdar 'you are divorce' unless the woman is a slave, then intention of three is valid. As for implicit forms, they occur only with intention in dianah, whether the context (mudhakarah) of divorce is present or not. Mudhakarah serves in place of intention only in qada' except the word 'haram': it is implicit but does not require intention; it refers to divorce if the husband is from a people who mean divorce by 'haram'. As for delegation of divorce, khul', ila', and zihar: what is explicit does not require intention; what is implicit requires it. As for ruj'a, it is like marriage because it is its continuation: what is explicit does not require intention; implicit requires it. As for oath by Allah: it does not depend on intention; it is contracted if he swears deliberately, forgetfully, mistakenly, or under coercion. Similarly if he does the sworn act likewise. As for intention to specify a general term in the oath, it is acceptable in dianah by agreement and in qada' according to al-Khassaf; fatwa is on his view if the swearer is oppressed. Also they differed: is consideration given to the intention of the swearer or the intention of the one who administers the oath? Fatwa is on...
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a detailed application of the principle that intention (niyyah) plays varying roles depending on the act. The author discusses the effect of intention across many chapters of Hanafi fiqh, showing when intention is required for validity, when only for reward, and when neither. The passage begins with udhiyah (sacrificial animal): intention determines whether the animal becomes specific to the sacrifice, with a distinction between poor and rich. For emancipation ('itq), the Hanafi position is that it is not inherently worship, so it is valid even without intention from a disbeliever, but intention brings reward. Implicit emancipation requires intention. Emancipation for an idol or Satan is valid but sinful if done by a Muslim. Jihad requires pure intention. Wills and waqf follow similar patterns. Marriage is considered a praiseworthy act that is valid even with jest, but intention is needed for reward. Judgment, hadd penalties, and testimony also depend on intention for reward. Permissible acts become worship through good intentions. Transactions like sale are generally valid without intention, except when using the present tense with immediate intent. Gift does not require intention for validity; coercion invalidates it due to lack of consent, unlike divorce and emancipation which occur under coercion. The section on divorce is extensive: explicit divorce occurs without intention even if mistaken, while implicit requires intention. The author clarifies that explicit divorce does not require intention for judicial effect (qada') but does for divine reward (dianah). Joking divorce is effective both judicially and religiously. The passage also covers specification of general oaths and the dispute between al-Khassaf and others. The overall message is that intention's role is nuanced and must be understood chapter by chapter.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intentional aim or purpose; legally, the determination to perform an act for a specific purpose.
صريح (sarih): Explicit wording that directly indicates the intended legal effect without need for context or intention.
كناية (kinayah): Implied or ambiguous wording that requires intention to determine the intended legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following acts does NOT require intention for its validity (sihhah)?
A) A marriage contracted with jest.
B) An explicit (sarih) divorce pronounced by a forgetful husband.
C) A sale contracted in the present tense (mudari') with immediate intent.
D) An oath to specify a general term in the court of conscience (dianah).

Key Takeaway
Intention's role in Hanafi fiqh is not monolithic: it determines reward for acts of worship, validates implicit contracts, and distinguishes between jest and seriousness, but explicit acts often stand without it.

beginner

The Definition and Purpose of Intention (Niyya)
Defines niyya and explains its purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the shar'i and linguistic definitions of niyya, explain its legislative purpose (tamyiz), and apply the definition to distinguish acts requiring intention.

Core Idea
Niyya distinguishes worship from habit; without it, an act remains custom.

Niyya (intention) is the heart's will directed toward an action to seek Allah's pleasure. Al-Qadi al-Baydawi's definition captures both the shar'i and linguistic dimensions. Understanding niyya is essential because it transforms mundane acts into acts of worship. In this lesson, we will define niyya and explore why the law mandated it.

Guided Path
1
1. Define niyya shar'an
Identify the shar'i definition: the will directed towards an action seeking Allah's face and obedience to His command.
From al-Qadi al-Baydawi.
2
2. Define niyya lughatan
Identify the linguistic definition: the heart's inclination towards what is perceived as beneficial or harm-repelling.
3
3. Explain the legislative purpose (tamyiz)
The law mandated niyya to distinguish acts of worship from mere customs (e.g., fasting vs. dieting) and to differentiate between types of worship (e.g., obligatory vs. supererogatory).
Source: al-Binaya and Fath al-Qadir.
4
4. Apply tamyiz to the case of refraining (tark)
Refraining from a prohibited act requires niyya only if the refraining becomes a positive act of obedience, not mere absence.
Tark without intention is not rewarded.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كفاء
ولا يرد عليه النيَّة في التروك لأنه كما قدَّمنا لا يتقرب بها إلا إذا صار الترك وهو فعل، وهو المكلّف به في النهي، لا الترك بمعنى العدم لأنه ليس داخلاً تحت القدرة للعبد كما في التحرير وعرَّفها القاضي البيضاوي بأنها شرعًا: الإرادة المتوجهة نحو الفعل ابتغاء لوجه الله تعالى وامتثالاً لحكمه. ولغة : انبعاث القلب نحو ما تراه موافقا لغرض من جلب نفع أو دفع ضرّ، حالاً أو مالاً. (انتهى). الثاني : بيان ما شرعت لأجله :
،
قالوا إن المقصود منها تمييز العبادات من العادات وتمييز بعض العبادات عن بعض كما في البناية وفتح القدير كالإمساك عن المفطرات، قد يكون حمية أو تداويًا أو لعدم الحاجة إليه، والجلوس في المسجد قد يكون للاستراحة، ودفع المال قد يكون هبة أو لغرض دنيوي، وقد يكون قربة كزكاة أو صدقة. والذبح قد يكون للأكل فيكون مُباحًا أو مندوبا ، أو للأضحية فيكون عبادة، أو لقدوم أمير فيكون حراما أو كفرًا على قول، ثم التقرب إلى الله تعالى يكون بالفرض والنفل والواجب، فشرعت لتمييزها عن بعضها .
،
فيفرع على ذلك؛ أن ما لا يكون إلا عبادة ولا يلتبس بغيره لا تشترط فيه، كالإيمان بالله تعالى كما قدَّمناه والمعرفة والخوف والرجاء والنية وقراءة القرآن والأذكار، لأنها متميّزة لا تلتبس بغيرها وما عدا الإيمان لم أره صريحًا ولكنه مخرج على الإيمان المصرَّح به ثم رأيت ابن وهبان في شرح المنظومة قال: إن ما لا يكون إلا عبادة لا يحتاج إلى النيَّة وذكر أيضًا أن النيَّة لا تحتاج إلى نيَّة. ونقل العيني في شرح البخاري الإجماع على أن التلاوة والأذكار والأذان لا يحتاج إلى نيَّة .
Kifa'. And niyya (intention) is not required in refraining (from actions), because as we have mentioned, one draws near (to Allah) through it only if the refraining becomes a (positive) act, and it is what one is obligated to do in the case of prohibitions, not refraining in the sense of non-existence, because that is not within the capacity of the servant, as in al-Tahrir. And al-Qadi al-Baydawi defined it (shar'an) as: the will directed towards an action seeking the face of Allah and obeying His command. And linguistically: the heart's inclination towards what it sees as agreeing with a purpose of obtaining benefit or repelling harm, present or future. (End). The second: Explanation of the purpose for which it (niyya) was legislated: They said that its objective is to distinguish acts of worship from customs, and to distinguish some acts of worship from others, as in al-Binaya and Fath al-Qadir. For example, refraining from things that break the fast may be due to diet, treatment, or lack of need; sitting in the mosque may be for rest; giving money may be a gift or for a worldly purpose, or it may be a good deed like zakat or charity; slaughtering may be for eating, making it permissible or recommended, or for sacrifice, making it worship, or for the arrival of an amir, making it forbidden or disbelief according to one view. Then drawing near to Allah may be obligatory, supererogatory, or necessary, so niyya was legislated to distinguish them from each other. Based on this: what is exclusively worship and not confused with anything else does not require niyya, like faith in Allah as we have mentioned, and (acts of) knowledge, fear, hope, intention (itself?), recitation of the Quran, and dhikr, because they are distinct and not confused with others. Apart from faith, I have not seen it explicitly, but it is derived from the explicit mention of faith. Then I saw Ibn Wahban in Sharh al-Man¬z¬uma say: that which is exclusively worship does not need niyya, and he also mentioned that niyya does not need niyya. Al-`Ayni in his commentary on al-Bukhari transmitted consensus that recitation, dhikr, and the adhan do not need niyya.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage begins by discussing the ruling of intention (niyya) in acts of refraining (tark). It clarifies that when a person refrains from a prohibited act, that refraining is considered a positive act of obedience if done with the right intention, as the capacity to refrain is within human ability. The passage then provides the definition of niyya according to al-Qadi al-Baydawi: it is the will directed toward an action seeking Allah's pleasure and compliance with His command. Linguistically, it is the heart's inclination toward something perceived as beneficial or harm-repelling. The second section explains the wisdom behind the legislation of niyya: to distinguish acts of worship from mere habits (e.g., fasting vs. dieting, sitting in mosque vs. resting), and to differentiate one act of worship from another (e.g., obligatory vs. supererogatory prayer). The passage then derives furu': acts that are exclusively worship and cannot be mistaken for habits do not require niyya. Examples include iman (faith), ma`rifa (knowledge of Allah), khawf (fear), raja' (hope), tilawa (Quran recitation), and adhkar (remembrances). Ibn Wahban is cited as stating that such acts do not need niyya, and al-`Ayni reports consensus that recitation, dhikr, and adhan do not require niyya. This is because these actions are inherently distinct and their worship aspect is self-evident.

Key Terms
النيَّة (al-niyya): The will directed towards an action seeking the face of Allah and obedience to His command (shar'an); the heart's inclination toward a perceived beneficial or harmful outcome (lughatan).
الترك (al-tark): Refraining from an action; it requires intention only when it becomes a positive act of obedience, not the mere absence of action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason intention (niyya) was legislated?
A) To make acts permissible.
B) To increase reward.
C) To distinguish worship from custom.
D) To ensure acts are valid.

Key Takeaway
Niyya is the heart's will that transforms a custom into worship by distinguishing it through intention.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
6 min
The Qawida: Acts Exclusively Worship Do Not Require Intention
Derives the qawida that exclusive worship acts do not need intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the qawida that certain acts do not require niyya, identify examples from the text, and apply the qawida to new cases.

Core Idea
Acts that are exclusively worship and unambiguous do not need intention.

The passage derives a crucial rule: acts that are inherently worship and cannot be mistaken for customs require no intention. This includes iman, recitation of Quran, dhikr, and adhan. Understanding this rule is vital for a mufti to know when intention is a condition.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the qawida
Locate the phrase 'ما لا يكون إلا عبادة لا يحتاج إلى النية' in the text.
It appears after 'فيفرع على ذلك'.
2
2. List the examples given
Faith, knowledge, fear, hope, recitation, dhikr, adhan.
Also niyya itself does not need intention (niyya does not need niyya).
3
3. Understand the reason (talil)
These acts are distinct and not confused with customs, so the need for tamyiz is absent.
4
4. Apply the qawida to a new case
For example, teaching Quran or giving a religious talk—are they exclusively worship? They may be mixed with worldly motives, so intention may be needed.
Not all purely religious acts are exclusive; some can be mixed.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
12 min
Specification in Intention: Container vs Measure
Explains when specification of the intended act is required in worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'Al-ta'yin fi al-muta'ayyin laghw' to determine whether specification of intention is required for a given act of worship.

Core Idea
Specification is needed when the time is a container; meaningless when the time exclusively determines the act.

What does it mean to intend a specific prayer or fast? The Hanafi school distinguishes between times that can accommodate multiple acts and times that exclusively define the act itself. This principle is captured by the sub-maxim 'Specification in the already determined is meaningless' (al-ta'yin fi al-muta'ayyin laghw). In this lesson, you will learn how to identify when intention must specify the act and when an absolute intention suffices, based on a detailed passage from Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time character: container (zarf) or measure (mi`yar)
Examine the time of the worship: can it accommodate other acts (e.g., Dhuhr time can include supererogatory prayers)? If yes, it is a container requiring specification. If the time is exclusive to one act (e.g., Ramadan for fasting), it is a measure where specification is not needed.
This is the foundational distinction driving the rule.
2
Apply the qawida: if measure, no specification; if container, specification required
Once the time character is identified, apply the legal maxim. For example, in Ramadan for a healthy resident, any intention (even supererogatory) suffices because the time itself determines the act. For prayer, you must specify which prayer (e.g., Dhuhr) because the time is a container.
Be careful: the qawida is 'specification in the already determined is meaningless'.
3
Handle exceptions: traveller, sick, ambiguous times
For a traveller in Ramadan, if he intends another obligation, it counts for that, not Ramadan. If he intends supererogation, the correct opinion is it counts for Ramadan. For Hajj, the time is ambiguous – treat it as a measure for absolute intention but as a container if supererogation is intended.
These exceptions show the interplay of intention and circumstance.
4
Apply to qada' (make-up) and tayammum
For qada' of prayers or fasts, specification is required unless the person cannot remember (e.g., intending 'first Dhuhr owed'). For tayammum, no need to distinguish between hadath and janaba; the purification suffices for any act because the condition is existence of purification, not specific intention.
These practical applications illustrate the limits of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : بيان تعيين المنوي وعدم تعيينه : الأصل عندنا أن المنوي؛ إما أن يكون من العبادات أو لا. فإن كان عبادة، فإن كان وقتها ظرفًا للمؤدي بمعنى أنه يسعه وغيره، فلا بد من التعيين. كالصلاة كأن ينوي الظهر، فإن قرنه باليوم كظهر اليوم صح، وإن خرج الوقت، أو بالوقت ولم يكن خرج الوقت فإن خرج ونسيه لا يجزئه في الصحيح، وفرض الوقت كظهر الوقت، إلا في الجمعة فإنها بدل لا أصل إلا أن يكون اعتقاده أنها فرض الوقت. فإن نوى الظهر لا غير، اختلفوا فيه والأصح الجواز. قالوا: وعلامة التعيين للصلاة بحيث يكون لو سئل أي صلاة يصلي يمكنه أن يجيب بلا تأمل. وإن كان وقتها معيارًا
لها، بمعنى أنه لا يسع غيرها كالصوم في ،رمضان كان معيارًا، فإن التعيين ليس بشرط، إن كان الصائم صحيحًا مقيمًا فيصح بمطلق النيَّة وبنيَّة النفل وواجب آخر لأن التعيين في المتعيّن لغو، وإن كان مريضًا ففيه روايتان والصحيح وقوعه عن رمضان، سواء نوى واجبًا آخر أو نفلاً. وأما المسافر، فإن نوى عن واجب آخر وقع عما نواه لا عن رمضان. وفي النفل روايتان والصحيح وقوعه عن رمضان، وإن كان وقتها مشكلاً كوقت الحج يشبه المعيار باعتبار أنه لا يصح في السنة إلا حجة واحدة، والظرف باعتبار أن أفعاله لا تستغرق وقته فيُصاب بمطلق النية نظرًا إلى المعيارية، وإن نوى نفلاً وقع عما نوى نظرًا إلى الظرفية ولا يسقط التعيين في الصلاة بضيق الوقت لأن السعة باقية؛ بمعنى أنه لو شرع متنفلاً وإن كان حراما. ولا يتعيَّن جزء من أجزاء الوقت بتعيين العبد قولاً، وإنما يتعين بفعله، كالحانث في اليمين لا يتعين واحد خصال الكفَّارة إلا في ضمن فعله هذا في الأداء. وأما في القضاء فلا بد من التعيين صلاة أو صومًا أو حجا.
من
وأما إذا كثرت الفوائت ؛ اختلفوا في اشتراط التعيين لتمييز الفروض المتحدة من جنس واحد والأصح أنه إن كان عليه قضاء من رمضان واحد، فصام يوما ناويا عنه، ولكن لم يعيّن أنه صام عن يوم كذا فإنه يجوز ولا يجوز في رمضانين ما لم يعيّن أنه صائم عن رمضان سنة كذا وأما قضاء الصلاة فلا يجوز ما لم يعين الصلاة ويومها بأن يعين ظهر يوم كذا. أو لو نوى أول ظهر عليه أو آخر ظهر عليه جاز، وهذا هو المخلص لمن لم يعرف الأوقات الفائتة أو اشتبهت عليه أو أراد التسهيل على نفسه.
وذكر في المحيط أن نيَّة التعيين في الصلاة لم تشترط باعتبار أن الواجب مختلف ،متعدد بل باعتبار أن مراعاة الترتيب واجب عليه ولا يمكنه مراعاة الترتيب إلا بنيَّة ،التعيين، حتى لو سقط الترتيب بكثرة الفوائت يكفيه نية الظهر لا غير. وهذا مشكل. وما ذكره أصحابنا كقاضي خان وغيره خلافه، وهو المعتمد
كذا في التبيين.
وقالوا في التيمم لا يجب التمييز بين الحدث والجنابة حتى لو تيمم الجنب يريد به الوضوء جاز خلافًا للخصاف، لكونه يقع لهما على صفة واحدة، فيميز بالنية كالصلوات المفروضة قالوا وليس بصحيح لأن الحاجة إليها ليقع طهارة، وإذا وقع طهارة جاز أن يؤدّي به ما شاء، لأن الشروط يُراعى وجودها لا غير. ألا ترى أنه لو تيمم للعصر جاز له أن يصلي به غيره.
•
٢٦
The third: Explanation of specification (ta'yin) of the intended act and when it is not required. The principle with us is that the intended act is either an act of worship or not. If it is worship, then if its time is a container (zarf) for the performance, meaning it accommodates both it and other (acts), then specification is necessary. Like prayer: one must intend Dhuhr. If he connects it with the day as 'Dhuhr of today', it is valid even if the time exits; or if he connects it with the time and the time has not exited, then if it exits and he forgot, it does not suffice according to the sound opinion. And the obligatory prayer of the time is like 'Dhuhr of the time', except for Friday prayer, because it is a substitute (badal) not an original, unless he believes it is the obligation of the time. If he intends merely 'Dhuhr' without more, there is a difference of opinion, and the soundest is permissibility. They said: the sign of specification for prayer is that if one is asked 'which prayer are you praying?' he can answer without hesitation. And if its time is a measure (mi`yar) in the sense that it does not accommodate anything else, like fasting in Ramadan is a measure, then specification is not a condition. If the fasting person is healthy and resident, then it is valid with absolute intention and with intention of supererogatory or another obligatory (fast), because specification in the already determined is meaningless. If he is sick, there are two narrations, and the correct opinion is that it occurs for Ramadan, whether he intended another obligation or supererogation. As for the traveller, if he intends another obligation, it occurs for what he intended, not for Ramadan. And regarding supererogation, there are two narrations, the correct opinion is that it occurs for Ramadan. And if the time is ambiguous (mushtakil), like the time of Hajj, it resembles both: the measure in that only one Hajj is valid per year, and the container in that its actions do not fill the entire time. So it suffices with absolute intention from the perspective of being a measure, but if he intends supererogation, it occurs for what he intended from the perspective of being a container. And specification in prayer is not dropped due to constriction of time because capacity remains; meaning that if he begins a supererogatory (prayer), it is haram. And a part of the time is not specified by the servant's statement, but rather by his action, like the one who breaks an oath: a single atonement option is not determined except by his action in performance. As for making up (qada'), specification is necessary, whether prayer, fasting, or Hajj. Then: if there are many missed (prayers/fasts), they differed on whether specification is required to distinguish the same type of obligations. The correct opinion is that if he owes make-up for one Ramadan and fasts a day intending it but does not specify which day, it is valid, but for two Ramadans it is not valid unless he specifies that he is fasting for the Ramadan of such-and-such year. As for making up prayers, it is not valid unless he specifies the prayer and its day, e.g., 'the Dhuhr of such-and-such day'. Or if he intends 'the first Dhuhr he owes' or 'the last Dhuhr he owes', it is valid. This is the solution for those who do not know the missed times or they are confused, or he wants to make it easy for himself. And it is mentioned in al-Muhit that the requirement of specification in prayer is not because the obligation is diverse or multiple, but because observing the order (tartib) is obligatory upon him, and he cannot observe order except by specification. So even if order is dropped due to many missed prayers, mere intention of Dhuhr suffices. This is problematic. What our companions like Qadi Khan and others mentioned is contrary to it, and it is relied upon. Thus in al-Tabyin. And they said regarding tayammum: distinguishing between minor impurity (hadath) and major impurity (janaba) is not required, such that if a junub person intends with tayammum to perform wudu', it is valid, contrary to al-Khassaf, because it falls upon both descriptions equally, and distinction is through intention like the obligatory prayers. They said it is not correct because the need is for purification to occur, and when purification occurs, it is permissible to perform any (act) with it, because conditions are only considered as to their existence, not otherwise. Do you not see that if one performs tayammum for `Asr, it is permissible for him to pray other (prayers) with it.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the third principle regarding intention: the requirement of specification (ta'yin) of the intended act in worship. It begins by stating the rule: if the time of a worship can accommodate other acts (like prayer times can include supererogatory prayers), then specification is necessary – e.g., one must intend Dhuhr, not just an unspecified prayer. If the time is exclusive to one act (like the month of Ramadan for fasting), then specification is not required; an absolute intention suffices, and even if one intends a supererogatory fast, it counts as Ramadan. Exceptions and nuances are given for the sick traveler, etc. The passage then discusses Hajj, whose time is ambiguous: it resembles an exclusive measure because only one Hajj per year, but also a container because the rites don't fill the entire time. The rule for qada' (make-up) is stricter: specification of the specific day and prayer is required, unless one intends 'the first owed' or similar. Finally, the passage addresses tayammum: no need to distinguish between hadath and janaba; if a junub person intends wudu' with tayammum, it is valid and the purification suffices for any worship. This is based on the principle that the condition is the existence of purification, not the specific intention. The text also notes a disagreement regarding the drop of specification due to many missed prayers: some say if order is dropped, mere intention suffices, but the relied-upon position is that specification is still required.

Key Terms
التعيين (al-ta'yin): Specification of the intended act of worship (e.g., which prayer, which day's fast) in the intention.
الظرف (al-zarf): A time that can contain multiple different acts (e.g., the time of Dhuhr can include other prayers).
المعيار (al-mi`yar): A time that exclusively determines one specific act (e.g., Ramadan determines the fast).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a healthy resident person who fasts in Ramadan intending a supererogatory fast?
A) The fast is invalid because intention must be for Ramadan.
B) The fast counts as supererogatory, not Ramadan.
C) The fast counts as the Ramadan fast because the time is a measure.
D) The fast is valid only if he also intends to make up a missed fast.

Key Takeaway
The key to whether specification (ta'yin) is required lies in the character of the time: container (zarf) demands specification, measure (mi`yar) renders specification unnecessary, except when intention definitively points elsewhere (like a traveller intending another obligation).

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate

The Principle of Specification in Worship: التعيين لتمييز الأجناس
Establishes the rule for specification in worship across multiple genres

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'Specification is to distinguish between types' to determine when intention must specify an act of worship and when absolute intention suffices.

Core Idea
Specification is needed only when obligations differ in their cause; within the same cause it is futile.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair establishes a foundational maxim for intention in worship. The Hanafi school teaches that specification (ta'yin) in intention is not an end in itself but a tool to distinguish different genres of obligations. The key is identifying the cause (sabab) that generates the obligation. When missed prayers or fasts arise from the same cause, absolute intention suffices; when causes differ, specification becomes necessary. This lesson unpacks the maxim and its practical applications across fasting, prayer, tayammum, expiations, and zakat.

Guided Path
1
Understand the maxim and its rationale
The maxim 'التعيين لتمييز الأجناس' means that specification (ta'yin) in intention is only needed to distinguish between different types (ajnas) of obligations. Within a single type, specification is futile because the act is already determined by its context.
Example: a healthy resident fasting in Ramadan does not need to intend 'Ramadan' – any intention suffices because the day itself is Ramadan.
2
Identify the criterion for different types: the cause (sabab)
The passage states that difference in type is known by difference in cause. The cause is the factor that makes an obligation required (e.g., time for prayer, month for fasting). Acts with the same cause belong to the same genre; acts with different causes are different genres.
Two Zuhr prayers from different days have different causes (different times), so they are different genres.
3
Apply to fasting: same cause vs. different causes
Fasts of Ramadan have one cause: the month of Ramadan. Therefore, within one Ramadan, specification is not needed. If missing fasts from two Ramadans, the cause differs (different years), so specification of the year is required.
The passage permits qada without specification from one Ramadan but requires it for two.
4
Apply to prayer: the role of order
Each prayer has its own time-based cause, so specification is normally required (prayer and day). However, if order is dropped due to many missed prayers, specifying just the prayer type (e.g., Zuhr) suffices. The relied-upon view still requires day specification, but the maxim's logic allows easing.
The text notes a difference of opinion; the mufta bihi is that specification of day is still needed.
5
Analyze the tayammum dispute
The Hanafi school holds that tayammum is one genre regardless of the state (hadath or janaba) because the need is purification. Specification is not needed. Al-Khassaf disagrees, but the Hanafi view relies on the maxim: the cause (need for purification) is the same.
Practical effect: a junub who performs tayammum intending wudu is still purified for both.
6
Extend to expiations and zakat
Within one type of expiation (e.g., multiple similar acts), no specification needed. Across different types (e.g., zakat on two properties), specification becomes necessary. Zakat prepayment has specific rules based on time and ownership.
The passage gives detailed zakat examples; the maxim governs the general principle.

Source Text

يوم كذا. أو لو نوى أول ظهر عليه أو آخر ظهر عليه جاز، وهذا هو المخلص لمن لم يعرف الأوقات الفائتة أو اشتبهت عليه أو أراد التسهيل على نفسه. وذكر في المحيط أن نيَّة التعيين في الصلاة لم تشترط باعتبار أن الواجب مختلف متعدد بل باعتبار أن مراعاة الترتيب واجب عليه ولا يمكنه مراعاة الترتيب إلا بنيَّة التعيين، حتى لو سقط الترتيب بكثرة الفوائت يكفيه نية الظهر لا غير. وهذا مشكل. وما ذكره أصحابنا كقاضي خان وغيره خلافه، وهو المعتمد كذا في التبيين. وقالوا في التيمم لا يجب التمييز بين الحدث والجنابة حتى لو تيمم الجنب يريد به الوضوء جاز خلافًا للخصاف، لكونه يقع لهما على صفة واحدة، فيميز بالنية كالصلوات المفروضة قالوا وليس بصحيح لأن الحاجة إليها ليقع طهارة، وإذا وقع طهارة جاز أن يؤدّي به ما شاء، لأن الشروط يُراعى وجودها لا غير. ألا ترى أنه لو تيمم للعصر جاز له أن يصلي به غيره. ضابط في هذا المبحث : التعيين لتمييز الأجناس : فنيَّة التعيين في الجنس الواحد لغو لعدم الفائدة. والتصرّف إذا لم يصادف محله كان لغوّا، ويعرف اختلاف الجنس باختلاف السبب. والصلاة كلها من قبيل المختلف؛ حتى الظهرين من يومين أو العصرين من يومين، بخلاف أيام رمضان فإنه يجمعها شهود الشهرة. ويفرّع على ذلك أنه لو كان عليه قضاء يوم بعينه فصامه بنية يوم آخر، أو كان عليه قضاء صوم يومين أو أكثر فصام يوما عن قضاء يومين جاز، بخلاف ما إذا نوى عن رمضانين، حيث لا يجوز لاختلاف السبب، كما إذا نوى ظهرين أو ظهرًا عن عصر، أو نوى ظهر يوم السبت وعليه ظهر يوم الخميس. وعلى هذا أداء الكفارات لا يحتاج إلى التعيين في جنس واحد، ولو عين لغى. وفي الأجناس لا بد منه، كما حققناه في الظهار من شرح الكنز، وأما في الزكاة فقالوا لو عجل خمسة سودًا عن مائتي درهم سود فهلكت السود قبل الحول وعنده نصاب آخر كان المعجل عن الباقي. وفي فتح القدير من الصوم ولو وجب عليه قضاء يومين من رمضان واحد؛ فالأولى أن ينوي أول أول يوم وجب عليه قضاؤه من هذا الرمضان، وإن لم يعين جاز. وكذا لو كانا من رمضانين على المختار حتى لو نوى القضاء لا غير جاز، ولو وجبت عليه كفَّارة فطر فصام إحدى وستين يوما عن القضاء والكفَّارة ولم يعين يوم القضاء جاز. وفي الخانية: لو عجَّل الزكاة عن أحد المالين فاستحق ما عجل عنه قبل الحول، لم يكن المعجّل عن الباقي، وكذا لو استحق بعد الحول لأن في الاستحقاق عجل عمَّا لم يكن في ملكه فيبطل التعجيل. (انتهى). وفيها أيضًا: لو كان له خمس من الإبل الحوامل يعني الحبالى، فعجل شاتين عنها وعما في بطونها ثم نتجت خمسًا قبل الحول أجزأه عما عجل، وإن عجل عما تحمل في السنة الثانية لا يجوز هذا كله في الفرائض والواجبات، كالمنذور والوتر على قول الإمام والعيد على الصحيح، وركعتي الطواف على المختار وينوي الوتر، لا الوتر الواجب للاختلاف فيه وفي صلاة الجنازة ينوي الصلاة لله تعالى والدعاء للميت. ولا يلزمه التعيين في سجود التلاوة لأي تلاوة سجد لها، كما في القنية. وأما النوافل فاتفق أصحابنا أنها تصح بمطلق النيَّة. وأما السنن الرواتب فاختلفوا في اشتراط تعيينها. والصحيح المعتمد عدم الاشتراط وأنها تصح بنية النفل وبمطلق النية.
There is a principle: specification is to distinguish between different types. So the intention of specification within the same type is futile due to lack of benefit. An action that does not encounter its proper locus is futile. The difference in type is known by difference in cause. All prayers are of the differing type; even two Zuhr prayers from two different days or two Asr prayers from two days, unlike the days of Ramadan which are unified by the sighting of the month. It is derived from this that if one owes the qada of a specific day and fasts it with the intention of another day, or owes the qada of two or more days and fasts one day with the intention of two days, it is permissible, contrary to if he intends for two Ramadans, where it is not permissible due to difference of cause, just as if he intends two Zuhr prayers or Zuhr prayer instead of Asr, or intends Zuhr of Saturday while owing Zuhr of Thursday. Accordingly, the performance of expiations does not require specification within one type, and if he specifies it is futile. But in different types it is necessary, as we have verified in the chapter on zihar from Sharh al-Kanz. Regarding zakat, they said: if he paid five black dirhams in advance for two hundred black dirhams, then the black dirhams perished before the year, and he had another nisab, the advance payment is considered for the remaining (property). In Fath al-Qadir on fasting: if he owes qada of two days from one Ramadan, it is better that he intend the first day of the days he owes from this Ramadan, and if he does not specify it is permissible. Similarly if they are from two Ramadans according to the chosen position, even if he intends only qada it is permissible. If he owes a kaffara for breaking a fast and fasts sixty-one days intending both qada and kaffara but does not specify the day of qada, it is permissible. In al-Khaniyya: if one pays zakat in advance for one of two properties, then the property for which he paid becomes due before the year, it is not considered as payment for the remaining property. Similarly if it becomes due after the year, because in the case of ownership being established, he paid in advance for what was not in his ownership, so the advance payment is void. (End). Also in it: if one has five pregnant camels, and pays two sheep in advance for them and for what is in their wombs, then they give birth to five before the year, it suffices for what he paid in advance. But if he pays in advance for what they will carry in the second year, it is not permissible. All this applies to obligatory acts and duties, such as vowed prayers, witr according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the Eid prayer according to the correct view, and the two rak'ats of tawaf according to the chosen view. One should intend witr, not the obligatory witr due to difference of opinion. In the funeral prayer, one intends the prayer for Allah and the supplication for the deceased. He is not required to specify in the prostration of recitation for which recitation he prostrated, as in al-Qunya. As for supererogatory prayers, our companions unanimously agree that they are valid with absolute intention. As for the regular sunnah prayers, they differed on the requirement of specification. The correct and relied-upon view is that it is not required, and they are valid with the intention of nafl and with absolute intention.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi rule regarding the requirement of specification (ta'yin) in acts of worship, derived from the maxim 'Specification is to distinguish between different types.' The author begins by clarifying that within a single type (jins wahid), specification is futile because there is no practical distinction to be made. For example, the fast of Ramadan is a specific time-bound obligation; a resident healthy person needs only an absolute intention or even an intention of nafl or another wajib, because the fast of Ramadan is already determined. However, for a sick person there are two narrations, the correct one being that it counts for Ramadan regardless of intention. A traveler intending another wajib counts for what he intended, not Ramadan. For a traveler intending nafl, there are two narrations, the correct one being that it counts for Ramadan. The passage then discusses prayer: specification is not dropped due to narrowness of time, because capacity remains; one cannot engage in nafl if it would invalidate the obligatory prayer. In qada prayers, specification is necessary: one must specify the prayer and its day. But if one owes many missed prayers, the requirement of order is dropped, and then specifying just the prayer type (e.g., Zuhr) suffices. However, the author notes that this is problematic, and the relied-upon position from Qadi Khan and others is that even then specification of the specific day is needed. The passage then addresses tayammum: no need to distinguish between hadath and janaba because tayammum is one and the same; if a junub performs tayammum intending wudu, it is valid, contrary to al-Khassaf. The proof: the need is for purification, and once purification is achieved, any prayer can be performed. The maxim is then formally stated: specification is to distinguish different types. Difference in type is known by difference in cause. All prayers are of different types even within the same genre, e.g., two Zuhr prayers from different days. But days of Ramadan are unified because they share a single cause (the month). Applications follow: if one owes a specific missed day and fasts it with intention of another day, or owes two days and fasts one day with intention of two, it is permissible. If one intends two Ramadans, it is not permissible due to difference of cause. The same applies to expiations: within one type, no specification needed; cross-type, it is required. Zakat prepayment rules are detailed. The passage concludes with rulings on supererogatory acts: all agree supererogatory prayers are valid with absolute intention; regular sunnah prayers have a difference, but the relied-upon view is that specification is not required.

Key Terms
التعيين (al-ta'yin): Specifying the specific act or type in intention
الجنس (al-jins): The type or category of obligation determined by its cause (sabab)
السبب (al-sabab): The cause that necessitates the obligation
التمييز (al-tamyiz): Distinguishing one obligation from another by specifying in intention

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the criterion for determining whether two obligations belong to the same genre (jins) for the purpose of specification in intention?
A) The time of day they are performed.
B) The cause (sabab) that necessitates the obligation.
C) The name of the act (e.g., prayer or fast).
D) Whether they are fard or wajib.

Key Takeaway
Specification in intention is only required to distinguish between obligations whose causes differ; within the same cause, absolute intention suffices.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
advanced
12 min
The Rule of Ta'yin (Specification) in Acts of Worship
Dar al-Mukhtar's rule on when specification is required in worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida of ta'yin to determine when intention must be specified in acts of worship and state the relied-upon view for sunan rawatib.

Core Idea
Specification distinguishes different types of worship; within the same type, it is futile.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi legal maxim that specification (ta'yin) serves only to separate different categories (ajnas) of worship. Understanding this rule clarifies when a worshipper must expressly name the act in intention and when a general intention suffices. We will examine the maxim's foundation, its application across ibadat, and the important exception for sunan rawatib and taraweeh.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida and its meaning
Begin by articulating the core maxim: 'Specification is for distinguishing types; specification within one type is futile due to lack of benefit.' Understand that an action that does not find its locus (the intended specific act) is futile.
The key is identifying what constitutes a 'type' (jins).
2
Identify the cause that defines a jins
Difference in type is known by difference in cause (sabab). For example, two Zuhr prayers on different days are of different types because each day is a separate cause. Conversely, the days of Ramadan share a single cause (the month), so they are of one type.
Always ask: what is the sabab that necessitates this worship?
3
Apply the qawida to furuat
Work through the branches: fasting qada days from the same Ramadan (same jins) requires no specification; from different Ramadans (different jins) requires specification. For zakat, advancing payment for one of two properties: if the property is lost, the payment does not apply to the other because the intended locus is gone.
Focus on how the sabab determines the jins.
4
Note the exceptions: sunan rawatib and taraweeh
The relied-upon view is that specification is not required for sunan rawatib and taraweeh; they are valid with absolute intention. This is an exception to the general rule for obligatory acts.
The exception is based on analogy with nafl and ease for the community.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf for sunan rawatib
Consider the practical consequence: on the relied-upon view, if one prays a sunna rawatib without specifying, it is valid. On Qadi Khan's opposite view, it would need to be repeated. Understand why the relied-upon view prevails.
This illustrates how ikhtilaf affects practice.

Source Text
