Combining Intentions: The Rule of Wasail and Maqasid
Maxim with initial furu' and istithna

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida on combining intentions to distinguish between means and ends, and state when combination is valid or invalid.

Core Idea
Combining intentions is valid for means but invalid for two obligatory prayers.

In Hanafi legal theory, intentions (niyyah) are central to acts of worship. A common question is whether a single intention can serve two acts. This lesson examines the rule from Ibn Nujaym's Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, which distinguishes between acts that are means (wasail) and those that are ends (maqasid). Understanding this distinction is crucial for a mufti faced with questions about overlapping worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The passage divides acts of worship into two categories: means (wasail) and ends (maqasid). Means are acts that are not the ultimate goal but a prerequisite, like ghusl for purification. Ends are the intended acts themselves, like prayers.
2
Apply the rule for means
The rule states that combining intentions in means is valid. Study the given example: a junub person performs ghusl both for Friday ghusl (sunnah) and to lift janabah (obligatory). The single ghusl fulfills both because ghusl is a means.
The Arabic: 'فإن الكل صحيح' (all of it is valid).
3
Analyze the first case of ends: two obligatory prayers
When the combination is in ends, the first sub-case is two obligatory acts. If they are prayers, the combination is invalid. The passage cites al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: neither prayer is valid because each has a distinct cause (sabab) and time.
The exception (istithna) to the general rule for ends is provided in the qawida panel.
4
Articulate the complete qawida
Synthesize the maxim: 'Combining two acts of worship: if in means, it is valid; if in ends, there is detail.' Then add the dabt (restriction): 'It is not valid for two obligatory prayers.'
This matches the qawida from the analytical toolbox.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادس : في بيان الجمع بين عبادتين : وحاصله : إما أن يكون في الوسائل، أو في المقاصد فإن كان في الوسائل فإن الكل صحيح : قالوا لو اغتسل الجنب يوم الجمعة للجمعة ولرفع الجنابة ارتفعت جنابته وحصل له ثواب غسل الجمعة وإن كان في المقاصد؛ فإما أن ينوي فرضين أو نفلين، أو فرضًا ونفلاً أما الأول؛ فلا يخلو إما أن يكون في الصلاة أو في غيرها، فإن كان في الصلاة لم تصح واحدة منهما . قال في السراج الوهاج : لو نوى صلاتي
Sixth: On Explaining Combining Two Acts of Worship: Its summary: Either it is in means or in ends. If it is in means, then all is valid: They said: If a junub person performs ghusl on Friday for Friday (prayer) and for lifting ritual impurity, his impurity is lifted and he obtains the reward of Friday ghusl. And if it is in ends, then either he intends two obligatory acts or two supererogatory acts, or an obligatory and a supererogatory act. As for the first (two obligatory): It is either in prayer or in other than prayer. If in prayer, neither of them is valid. He said in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If he intends two prayers...
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This is the sixth section on combining two acts of worship with a single intention. The author (Ibn Nujaym) summarizes the rule: If the combination is in means (wasail), i.e., acts that are means to an end, then it is valid (kulluhu sahih). The example given is a junub person performing ghusl (ritual bath) on Friday with the intention of both the Friday ghusl (sunnah) and lifting the state of janabah (obligatory). Both intentions are fulfilled: he becomes pure and gets the reward of Friday ghusl. This is because ghusl is a means to an end (purification and sunnah), and the single act suffices for both. If the combination is in ends (maqasid), i.e., the acts themselves are the intended worship, then there are three cases: (1) two obligatory acts (fardayn), (2) two supererogatory acts (naflayn), or (3) one obligatory and one supererogatory (fard wa nafal). The passage only begins to discuss the first case: if in prayer, neither is valid. This is because each prayer has a distinct intention and time/cause, and one intention cannot cover two distinct obligatory prayers. The source cited is al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. The text ends abruptly at 'If he intends two prayers...' indicating the rest of the discussion continues on the next page.

Key Terms
الوسائل (al-wasa'il): Acts that are means to an end, not the end itself, such as ghusl which is a means to purification and a sunnah act.
المقاصد (al-maqasid): The intended acts of worship themselves, such as prayers, fasting, etc. that are ends in themselves.
الجمع (al-jam'): Combining two acts of worship under a single intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi qawida, a person performs ghusl on Friday with the intention of both the Friday ghusl (sunnah) and lifting the state of janabah. What is the ruling?
A) The ghusl is valid only for the sunnah, not for janabah.
B) The ghusl is invalid because he combined two intentions.
C) The ghusl is valid for both; janabah is lifted and he gets reward for Friday ghusl.
D) The ghusl is valid only for janabah because that is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, combining intentions is valid for means (wasail) but invalid for two obligatory prayers (maqasid), each requires its own intention.

Subsidiary Intentions in Jihad and Hajj
Applying the intention maxim to jihad and Hajj cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of tabi'iyyah to determine when a secondary worldly intention does not invalidate an act of worship in the cases of jihad and Hajj.

Core Idea
A secondary worldly intention does not harm the primary religious goal if the primary intent is sincere.

This lesson explores how the Hanafi school distinguishes between dominant and subsidiary intentions in acts of worship, using the examples of the market-person in jihad and the pilgrim who trades. The key is whether the worldly motive is the primary driver or merely incidental.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary act
Determine the act of worship being performed: jihad or Hajj.
2
Identify the worldly intention
Identify the secondary worldly goal: trade or seeking a debtor.
3
Assess dominance
Decide whether the worldly intention is primary or subsidiary based on evidence of action (e.g., fighting in jihad, standing at Arafat).
Fighting reveals true intention; mere travel without fighting shows primary intent for trade.
4
Apply the maxim
Use the qa'idah 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to derive the ruling: if primary intent is religious, subsidiary intent does not harm reward or validity.
5
Distinguish tawaf from wuquf
Note that tawaf is not the essential pillar, so a worldly intent (seeking debtor) invalidates it; wuquf is the essential pillar, so the worldly intent is subsidiary and does not invalidate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا ينبغي أن يترك. وفي الولوالجية : إذا أراد أن يصلي أو يقرأ القرآن فيخاف أن يدخل عليه الرياء، يترك لأنه أمر موهوم. (انتهى). وصرَّحوا في كتاب السير بأن السوقي لا أجر له لأنه عند المجاوزة لم يقصد إلا التجارة لا إعزاز الدين وإرهاب العدو، فإن قاتل استحق لأنه ظهر بالمقاتلة أنه قصد القتال والتجارة تبع فلا تضره، كالحاج إذا اتجر في طريق الحاج لا ينقص أجره. ذكره الزيلعي وظاهره أن الحاج إذا خرج تاجرًا فلا أجر له وصرَّحوا بأنه لو طاف طالبًا غريمه لا يجزئه ولو وقف بعرفة طالبًا غريمه أجزأه والفرق ظاهر وقالوا لو فتح المصلي على غير إمامه بطلت صلاته لقصد التعليم. ورأيت فرعًا في بعض كتب الشافعية رضي الله عنهم، حكاه النووي فيمن قال له إنسان : صلِّ الظهر ولك دينار، فصلى بهذه النيَّة، أنها تجزئه صلاته ولا يستحق الدينار (انتهى). ولم أرَ مثله لأصحابنا. وينبغى على قواعدنا أن يكون كذلك. أما الإجزاء فلما قدمنا أن الرياء لا يدخل الفرائض في حق سقوط الواجب، وأما عدم استحقاق الدينار فلأن أداء الفرائض لا يدخل تحت عقد الإجارة ; ألا ترى إلى قولهم : لو استأجر الأب ابنه للخدمة لا أجر له؟ ذكره البزازي لأن الخدمة عليه واجبة. بل أفتى المتقدمون بأن العبادات لا تصح الإجارة عليها كالإمامة والأذان وتعليم القرآن والفقه لكن المعتمد ما أفتى به المتأخرون من الجواز. وقدمنا أنه إذا نوى الإعتاق لرجل كان مباحًا . وأما عدم . ولم أر حكم ما إذا نوى الصوم والحمية ويشملها ما إذا أشرك بين عبادة وغيرها، فهل تصح العبادة؟ وإذا صحت هل يُثاب بقدره أو لا ثواب له أصلا؟ وأما الخشوع فيها بظاهره وباطنه فمستحب وفي القنية ; شرع في الفرض وشغله الفكر في التجارة أو المسألة حتى أتم صلاته لا يستحبّ إعادته وفي بعض الكتب لا يُعيد وفي بعضها لا ينقص أجره إذا لم يكن من تقصير منه .
So it should not be left. And in al-Walwaljiyya: If he wants to pray or read the Quran and fears that riya' (ostentation) may enter upon him, he leaves it because it is an imagined matter. (End). And they explicitly stated in the book of Siyar that the market-person has no reward because when passing by he intended only trade, not glorifying the religion and intimidating the enemy. If he fights, he deserves because by fighting it becomes apparent that he intended fighting, and trade is subsidiary and does not harm him, like the pilgrim if he trades on the way of pilgrimage, his reward is not diminished. Al-Zayla'i mentioned it and its apparent meaning is that if the pilgrim goes out as a trader, he has no reward. And they explicitly stated that if he performs tawaf seeking his debtor, it is not valid; and if he stands at Arafat seeking his debtor, it is valid for him, and the difference is apparent. And they said: If the worshiper corrects (opens) someone other than his imam, his prayer is invalidated due to intending teaching. And I saw a branch in some Shafi'i books, narrated by al-Nawawi, concerning a man who said to another: Pray Zuhr and you will have a dinar, and he prayed with this intention, that his prayer is valid and he does not deserve the dinar. (End). And I have not seen the like for our companions. And according to our principles it should be like that. As for validity, because we mentioned that riya' does not enter the obligatory acts regarding the dropping of the obligation. And as for not deserving the dinar, because performing obligatory acts does not fall under a contract of hire; do you not see their statement: If a father hires his son for service, he has no reward? Al-Bazzazi mentioned it because service is obligatory upon him. Rather, the early scholars gave fatwa that hiring for acts of worship is not valid, like imamate, adhan, teaching Quran and fiqh, but the relied-upon is what the later scholars gave fatwa of permissibility. And we mentioned that if he intended freeing a slave for a man, it is permissible. And as for non-... And I have not seen the ruling if he intends fasting and dieting, and it includes if he associates between worship and other things: is the worship valid? If valid, is he rewarded proportionally or has no reward at all? And as for khushu' in it, outwardly and inwardly, it is recommended. And in al-Qunyah: He began the obligatory prayer and his thought preoccupied him with trade or a question until he completed his prayer; its repetition is not recommended. In some books: he does not repeat. In some: his reward is not diminished if it was not due to his negligence.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage presents several applications of the maxim 'Actions are judged by intentions' (الأمور بمقاصدها). It begins by stating that one should not abandon an act of worship merely due to a fear of riya' (ostentation), because such fear is based on an uncertain possibility (amr mawhum). The text then discusses the market-person (al-suqi) who joins a military expedition: if his primary intention is trade, not jihad, he receives no reward; if he fights, his fighting shows his true intention, and trade becomes subsidiary, so he is rewarded. Similarly, a pilgrim who trades during Hajj does not lose his reward because trade is subsidiary. However, if one goes out primarily as a trader, the apparent view is that he gets no Hajj reward. The ruling distinguishes between tawaf (circumambulation) and wuquf at Arafat: if one performs tawaf seeking a debtor, it does not count as worship, but standing at Arafat with the same intention does, because the latter is the essential pillar. Correcting (فتح) someone other than one's imam in prayer invalidates the prayer if done to teach, as teaching is a worldly intent. A Shafi'i branch discusses a man told to pray Zuhr for a dinar; his prayer is valid but he does not deserve the dinar because obligatory acts cannot be hired. Hanafi scholars agree, noting that hiring for worship (imamate, adhan, teaching) was initially invalid but later scholars permitted it. The passage further explores mixing worship with dieting (himiya) and whether reward is given. It concludes that khushu' is recommended, and that distraction in prayer due to trade thoughts does not necessitate repetition and does not diminish reward if unintentional.

Key Terms
السوقي (al-suqi): A person who goes out for jihad primarily for trade, not for religious purposes.
التبعية (al-tabi'iyyah): The principle that a subsidiary intention (e.g., trade) does not harm the primary intention (e.g., worship) if it is not the main goal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the difference between tawaf and wuquf at Arafat when performed with a worldly intention (seeking a debtor)?
A) Both are invalid because worldly intent negates worship.
B) Tawaf is invalid, but wuquf is valid because wuquf is the essential pillar.
C) Tawaf is valid, but wuquf is invalid because tawaf is more important.
D) Both are valid because worldly intent is always subsidiary.

Key Takeaway
A secondary worldly intention does not invalidate worship or diminish reward if the primary religious intent is dominant and the act's essential pillars are fulfilled.

Riya', Correcting in Prayer, Hiring for Worship, and Mixed Intentions
Applying the intention maxim to riya', teaching, hire, and mixed intentions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between cases where worldly intentions in worship affect validity versus those that affect only reward, and apply the Hanafi position on hiring for acts of worship.

Core Idea
Worldly intentions in worship vary: some invalidate the act, others only reduce reward; hiring for worship is now permissible per later Hanafi fatwa.

This lesson continues applying the intention maxim to several nuanced cases: fear of riya', correcting someone else's prayer, praying for monetary reward, hiring for worship, mixing fasting with dieting, and distraction in prayer. The rulings illustrate how the Hanafi school carefully calibrates the effect of worldly motives on validity and reward.

Guided Path
1
Classify the worldly intent
Identify whether the worldly intent is primary or subsidiary, and whether it relates to the validity or reward of the act.
2
Apply the ruling on riya'
Riya' in obligatory acts does not invalidate the obligation but may remove reward; fear of riya' should not lead to abandoning the act.
3
Analyze the corrective action in prayer
Correcting someone other than the imam for teaching purposes invalidates the prayer because teaching is a distinct worldly intent.
4
Evaluate the hire for worship issue
Early scholars disallowed hiring for worship; later scholars permitted it. The mufta bihi is the later position.
5
Consider mixed intentions and distraction
For acts like fasting with dieting or distraction in prayer, the ruling depends on whether the worldly intent dominates and whether it was intentional.

Key Terms
الرياء (al-riya'): Performing acts of worship to be seen by people, which invalidates the intention of sincerity.
التبعية (al-tabi'iyyah): The principle that a subsidiary intention (e.g., trade) does not harm the primary intention (e.g., worship) if it is not the main goal.
الخشوع (al-khushu'): Humility and concentration in prayer, which is recommended but not obligatory.

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on hiring for acts of worship (e.g., imamate, adhan, teaching Quran)?
A) It is absolutely invalid because it contradicts sincerity.
B) It is valid according to early scholars and invalid according to later scholars.
C) It was invalid according to early scholars but permissible according to later scholars, and the latter is the relied-upon position.
D) It is permissible only for teaching Quran but not for imamate.

Key Takeaway
Worldly intentions in worship vary in effect: some invalidate, some only reduce reward; and hiring for worship is now permissible according to the later Hanafi position.

Combining Two Acts of Worship: The Rules of Intention (الجمع بين عبادتين)
Classification of combining intentions in worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qa'idah for combining intentions in worship to determine which intent prevails in means, ends, and mixed cases.

Core Idea
In means, multiple intentions are valid; in ends, the stronger intent prevails; if equal, a choice is given.

When a worshipper intends two acts simultaneously, the legal outcome depends on whether the acts are means or ends. This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir systematically presents the Hanafi framework, covering cases from ghusl to prayer and fasting. By mastering this qa'idah, you will be able to resolve complex intention conflicts in worship.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish means from ends
Identify whether the acts are prerequisites (wasail) or ultimate objectives (maqasid). In means, combination is always valid.
E.g., ghusl is a means; Friday reward and janabah removal are both achieved.
2
Classify the pair of ends
Determine if the two intended acts are both obligatory, both voluntary, or one of each. The rules differ for each category.
Two obligatory ends in prayer are invalid by consensus; in fasting, the stronger prevails.
3
Apply strength comparison
If the two ends are both obligatory, compare their strength (e.g., qada' is stronger than kaffara; zakah is stronger than kaffarat al-yamin). The stronger intent prevails.
If equal, the person has a choice (e.g., two kaffaras).
4
Handle obligatory + voluntary
For one obligatory and one voluntary act, there is ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school: Abu Yusuf says the obligatory prevails; Muhammad says both are invalid. The mufta bihi is often Abu Yusuf's view.
This ikhtilaf appears in prayer and zakah cases.
5
Apply to voluntary + voluntary
When both acts are voluntary (e.g., tahiyyah and sunnah of Fajr), one intention suffices for both—both are achieved.
This is because there is no conflict of obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادس : في بيان الجمع بين عبادتين : وحاصله : إما أن يكون في الوسائل، أو في المقاصد فإن كان في الوسائل فكالكل صحيح : قالوا لو اغتسل الجنب يوم الجمعة للجمعة ولرفع الجنابة ارتفعت جنابته وحصل له ثواب غسل الجمعة وإن كان في المقاصد ; فإما أن ينوي فرضين أو نفلين، أو فرضًا ونفلاً أما الأول; فلا يخلو إما أن يكون في الصلاة أو في غيرها، فإن كان في الصلاة لم تصح واحدة منهما . قال في السراج الوهاج : لو نوى صلاتي فرض كالظهر والعصر، لم يصح اتفاقا ولو نوى في الصوم القضاء والكفّارة، كان عن القضاء. وقال محمد: يكون تطوّعًا. وإن نوى كفَّارة الظهار وكفارة اليمين يجعله لأيهما شاء. وقال محمد: يكون تطوعًا. ولو نوى الزكاة وكفارة الظهار جعله عن أيهما شاء ولو نوى الزكاة وكفَّارة اليمين فهو عن الزكاة ولو نوى مكتوبة وصلاة جنازة فهي عن المكتوبة. وقد ظهر بهذا أنه إذا نوى فرضين فإن كان أحدهما أقوى انصرف إليه . فصوم القضاء أقوى من صوم الكفَّارة، وإن استويا في القوة، فإن كان في الصوم فله الخيار ككفَّارة الظهار وكفَّارة اليمين وكذا الزكاة وكفَّارة الظهار. وأما كفَّارة اليمين فالزكاة أقوى وأما في الصلاة فيقدم الأقوى أيضًا، ولذا قدمنا المكتوبة على صلاة الجنازة ولذا قال في السراج الوهاج : لو نوى مكتوبتين فهي للتي دخل وقتها ولو نوى فائتتين فهي للأولى منهما، ولو نوى فائتة ووقتية فهي للفائتة؛ إلا أن يكون في آخر الوقت، ولو نوى الظهر والفجر وعليه الفجر من يومه فإن كان في أول وقت الظهر فهي عن الفجر، وإن كان في آخره فهي عن الظهر. (انتهى). بقي ما إذا كبر ناويًا للتحريمة وللركوع، وما إذا طاف للفرض والوداع، وإن نوى فرضًا ونفلاً، فإن نوى الظهر والتطوّع ; قال أبو يوسف: تجزئه عن المكتوبة ويبطل التطوّع. وقال محمد : لا تجزئه المكتوبة ولا التطوع وإن نوى الزكاة والتطوع يكون عن الزكاة. وعند محمد عن التطوّع، ولو نافلة وجنازة فهي نافلة، كذا في السراج. وأما إذا نوى نافلتين كما إذا نوى بركعتي الفجر التحية والسنة أجزأت عنهما. ولم أر حكم ما إذا نوى سنتين كما إذا نوى في يوم الاثنين صومه عنه، وعن يوم عرفة إذا وافقه ; فإن مسألة التحية إنما كانت ضمنًا للسنة لحصول المقصود.
The sixth: Explaining combining two acts of worship. Its summary is: either it is in means (wasail) or in ends (maqasid). If it is in means, then all are valid: they said if a junub person performs ghusl on Friday for Friday and for removing janabah, his janabah is removed and he attains the reward of Friday ghusl. If it is in ends, then either he intends two obligatory acts, two voluntary acts, or one obligatory and one voluntary. As for the first, it is either in prayer or in other than prayer. If it is in prayer, not one of them is valid. He said in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If he intends two obligatory prayers like Zuhr and Asr, it is not valid by agreement. And if he intends in fasting qada' and kaffara, it is for qada'. Muhammad said: It becomes voluntary. And if he intends kaffarat al-zihar and kaffarat al-yamin, he may apply it to whichever he wishes. Muhammad said: It becomes voluntary. And if he intends zakah and kaffarat al-zihar, he may apply it to whichever he wishes. And if he intends zakah and kaffarat al-yamin, it is for zakah. And if he intends an obligatory prayer and janazah prayer, it is for the obligatory. It has become apparent from this that if he intends two obligatory acts, if one is stronger, it prevails. Thus, qada' fast is stronger than kaffara fast; if they are equal in strength, in fasting he has a choice, like kaffarat al-zihar and kaffarat al-yamin, and likewise zakah and kaffarat al-zihar. As for kaffarat al-yamin, zakah is stronger. And in prayer, the stronger is also given precedence, thus we gave precedence to the obligatory prayer over janazah prayer. And thus he said in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If he intends two obligatory prayers, it is for the one whose time has entered; if he intends two missed prayers, it is for the earlier one; if he intends a missed prayer and a current prayer, it is for the missed one, except if at the end of the time; and if he intends Zuhr and Fajr while he owes Fajr from the same day, if in the early time of Zuhr it is for Fajr, if in the late time it is for Zuhr. (End). There remains: if he says takbir intending both tahrimah and ruku', and if he performs tawaf intending both obligatory and farewell, and if he intends an obligatory and a voluntary act: if he intends Zuhr and supererogatory, Abu Yusuf said: It suffices for the obligatory and the supererogatory is invalid. Muhammad said: Neither the obligatory nor the supererogatory suffices. If he intends zakah and supererogatory, it is for zakah; according to Muhammad, it is for supererogatory. If he intends nafl and janazah, it is nafl, as in al-Siraj. As for intending two voluntary acts, like if he intends with the two rak'ahs of Fajr both tahiyyah and sunnah, they suffice for both. And I have not seen the ruling if he intends two sunnahs, like if he intends on Monday to fast for it and for the day of Arafah if it coincides; for the issue of tahiyyah was implicitly for the sunnah due to achieving the objective.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a systematic exposition of the rules for combining two acts of worship in a single intention. It is from the chapter on 'Combining Two Acts of Worship' (الجمع بين عبادتين). The author divides the cases into two categories: combination in means (wasail) and combination in ends (maqasid). In means, like ghusl for both Friday and janabah, both objectives are achieved: janabah is removed and the reward of Friday ghusl is attained. In ends, further subdivision: two obligatory acts, two voluntary acts, or one obligatory and one voluntary. For two obligatory acts in prayer, they are invalid by agreement; in fasting, if one is stronger (e.g., qada' over kaffara), the stronger prevails; if equal (e.g., two kaffaras or zakah and kaffarat al-zihar), the person has a choice, except when the stronger is evident (zakah over kaffarat al-yamin). For prayer, precedence is given to the prayer whose time has entered. For combining obligatory and voluntary, there is ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. For two voluntary acts, like tahiyyat al-masjid and sunnah of Fajr, one intention suffices for both. This section is a thorough treatment of the qa'idah that intentions are judged by the predominant element, and when intentions conflict, the stronger or more specific prevails.

Key Terms
الوسائل (al-wasail): Means or prerequisites that are not themselves the ultimate objective of worship, e.g., ghusl for a condition of prayer.
المقاصد (al-maqasid): The ends or ultimate objectives of worship, e.g., the obligatory prayer itself.
القضاء والكفارة (al-qada' wa al-kaffara): Qada' is making up a missed obligatory fast; kaffara is an expiatory fast for certain violations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone intends to fast both the qada' of Ramadan and a kaffara fast, what is the ruling?
A) Both are invalid because two intentions conflict.
B) It counts as qada' fast because it is stronger.
C) It counts as kaffara fast because it is more specific.
D) He may choose which one it counts for.

Key Takeaway
Combining intentions in worship is often valid: in means all are valid, in ends the stronger prevails, and if equal a choice is given—except in prayer where two obligations cannot combine.

Multiple Ihrams for Hajj: The Qawida and Its Furuat
Rulings on entering multiple ihrams simultaneously or consecutively.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida regarding multiple ihrams to determine binding effect and timing of rafd, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf among Hanafi imams.

Core Idea
Two ihrams bind but one drops; timing of rafd determines penalty.

This passage from Fath al-Qadir and al-Mabsut presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute on entering multiple ihrams. The key qawida states that both ihrams are binding, but one is eventually dropped. However, the imams differ on when that dropping (rafd) occurs, and this timing affects the rulings on violations such as hunting and intercourse. Understanding this qawida and its exceptions is essential for a mufti issuing fatwas on complex Hajj scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core qawida
Find the Arabic statement of the maxim: 'إذا اجتمع إحرامان لزماه عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ويرتفض أحدهما' (If two ihrams combine, both are binding according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and one is dropped). This is the central rule of the lesson.
The qawida is a sughra (minor) maxim specific to the Hajj chapter.
2
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that Imam Muhammad disagrees: in simultaneity only one binds; in consecutiveness only the first binds. Also, among the majority, the timing of rafd differs between Abu Hanifa (at start of actions) and Abu Yusuf (immediately upon ihram).
This ikhtilaf is reflected in the madhhab_dispute_map.
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf for violations
Apply the differing timings to concrete cases: hunting before starting actions — Abu Hanifa says 2 dam, Abu Yusuf says 1 dam. For intercourse before actions — Abu Hanifa says 2 dam for intercourse + 1 dam for rafd; Abu Yusuf's ruling is implicit but presumably 1 dam.
The practical difference hinges on when the second ihram is considered dropped.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Al-Mabsut states that the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is zahir al-riwayah (the relied-upon transmission). The later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Kasani, al-Marghinani) prefer Abu Hanifa's timing for rafd (at start of actions).
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
5
Recognize the broader qawida for intention
The passage begins with a related rule: when ihram is entered for both a vow (nadhr) and a voluntary (nafl) Hajj, it counts as nafl; similarly, fard and tatawwu' counts as tatawwu'. This is based on the principle that the lesser obligation prevails over the greater? Actually here the voluntary supercedes the obligatory? The text says 'كان تطوّعا' — it becomes voluntary. This is counterintuitive but is an established rule in the school.
This part is separate from the two-ihram issue but falls under the same chapter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما التعدّد في الحج ; قال في فتح القدير من باب الإحرام: لو أحرم نذرًا ونفلاً كان نفلاً، أو فرضًا وتطوّعًا كان تطوّعًا عندهما في الأصح. ومن باب إضافة الإحرام إلى الإحرام لو أحرم بحجتين معًا أو على التعاقب الزماه عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، وعند محمد في المعية يلزمه إحداهما، وفي التعاقب الأولى فقط . وإذا لزماه عندهما ارتفضت إحداهما باتفاقهما لكن اختلفا في وقت الرفض; فعند أبي يوسف عند صيرورته محرمًا بلا مهلة وعند أبي حنيفة إذ شرع في الأعمال، وقيل إذا توجه سائرا . ونصّ في المبسوط على أنه ظاهر الرواية . وثمرة الخلاف فيما إذا جنى قبل الشروع فعليه دمان للجناية على إحرامين، ودم واحد عند أبي يوسف ولو جامع قبل الشروع فعليه دمان للجماع ودم ثالث للرفض،
As for multiplicity in Hajj: He said in Fath al-Qadir from the chapter of Ihram: If he enters ihram for a vow and a voluntary Hajj, it counts as voluntary; or for an obligatory and supererogatory Hajj, it counts as supererogatory according to both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) in the more correct view. And from the chapter of adding ihram to ihram: If he enters ihram for two Hajjs simultaneously or consecutively, both are binding upon him according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; according to Muhammad, in simultaneity one of them is binding, and in consecutiveness only the first. And if both are binding according to them, one of them is dropped by agreement, but they differed on the time of dropping: according to Abu Yusuf, when he becomes a muhrim without delay; according to Abu Hanifa, when he begins the actions; and it is said when he sets out traveling. And it is stated in al-Mabsut that it is the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah). The consequence of the ikhtilaf is: if he commits a hunting violation before starting (the actions), he owes two blood sacrifices for transgression against two ihrams, and according to Abu Yusuf, one blood sacrifice. And if he has intercourse before starting, he owes two blood sacrifices for intercourse and a third for dropping (the ihram).
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage addresses the rules when a person enters multiple ihrams (i.e., intends to perform multiple Hajjs) either simultaneously or consecutively. It is from the chapter on ihram in Fath al-Qadir. The author begins with a related rule: if one enters ihram for both a nadhr (vow) and a nafl (voluntary) Hajj, the latter dominates (it becomes nafl); similarly, if for fard and tatawwu', it becomes tatawwu' according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. This is based on the principle that the stronger (or here, the more voluntary) intention prevails. Then the main discussion: entering ihram for two Hajjs (e.g., two obligatory or two voluntary). According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, both ihrams are binding (لزماه), but one will eventually be dropped. According to Muhammad, only one is binding: in simultaneous intention, he has a choice; in sequential (e.g., intending a second Hajj after the first), only the first binds. If both bind, they agree one is dropped, but differ on when: Abu Yusuf says immediately upon becoming muhrim; Abu Hanifa says when he begins the actions (e.g., tawaf, sa'y); a third opinion says when he sets out traveling. Al-Mabsut states that this (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's view) is the reliable transmission (zahir al-riwayah). The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) appears in case of violations: if he hunts before starting actions, according to Abu Hanifa he owes two dam (blood sacrifices) for violating two ihrams; according to Abu Yusuf, only one dam because only one ihram is actually in effect. If he has intercourse before starting, according to Abu Hanifa he owes two dam for the intercourse (one for each ihram) and a third for dropping one ihram? The text says 'daman lil-jima' wa damun thalith li al-rafd' - two for intercourse and a third for dropping; according to Abu Yusuf, presumably different. This is a complex area of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or Umrah, entered by intention and talbiyah, involving prohibitions.
الرفض (al-rafd): The dropping or cancellation of one of two binding ihrams, occurring at a specific time.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted rulings from the founding Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) in the six core books of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if someone enters ihram for two Hajjs simultaneously and then hunts before starting the actions of Hajj, how many dam (blood sacrifices) are required?
A) One dam, because only one ihram is effective.
B) Two dams, one for each ihram violated.
C) Three dams, for two ihrams and the act of hunting.
D) No dam, because hunting is not yet a violation.

Key Takeaway
Two ihrams bind but one drops; the mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa's timing (at start of actions) and assesses penalties accordingly.

The Qawida on the Time of Intention for Prayer
Definition and application of the qawida on time of intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi qawida on the time of intention for prayer, distinguish between actual and legal concurrence, and apply it to determine the validity of a prayer when intention precedes the takbir.

Core Idea
Intention must be concurrent with the start of prayer, actually or legally; an earlier intention suffices if no unrelated act intervenes.

This passage defines a key qawida from the Hanafi school: intention must accompany the beginning of the act of worship. For prayer, this principle has nuances: an intention made earlier (e.g., at wudu) can be legally sufficient if not interrupted by unrelated acts. The passage also discusses a minority view that allows delay, which is rejected as weak.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qawida
The principle stated is that intention must be concurrent with the start of prayer, either actually or legally. The start is the takbir (tahrimah).
Concurrence can be actual (at the moment) or legal (earlier intention persists).
2
Understand legal concurrence
Legal concurrence occurs when an intention made earlier (e.g., at wudu) remains valid if the person does not engage in an act unrelated to prayer before starting.
Acts like walking to the mosque are considered from the genus of prayer and do not break the intention.
3
Apply to the given scenario
According to Imam Muhammad, Abu Hanifa, and Abu Yusuf, if one intends Dhuhr at wudu and goes to the mosque without speaking, eating, etc., the earlier intention suffices.
The condition is that nothing from outside the genus of prayer occurs.
4
Analyze the dispute
Some mashayikh (e.g., al-Karkhi) allowed delaying intention after takbir, but these views are deemed weak. The relied-upon view is concurrence.
The reason for rejection: the first part of prayer would lack intention, and intention is indivisible.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi position is that intention must be concurrent with the start, either actually or legally. The minority views are not adopted.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابع: في وقتها
الأصل أن وقتها أول العبادات ولكن الأول حقيقي وحكمي، فقالوا في الصلاة لو نوى قبل الشروع؛ فعند محمد لو نوى عند الوضوء أنه يصلي الظهر أو العصر مع الإمام ولم يشتغل بعد النيَّة بما ليس من جنس الصلاة إلا أنه لما انتهى إلى مكان الصلاة لم تحضر النيَّة، جازت صلاته بتلك النيَّة، وهكذا رُوِيَ عن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، كذا في الخلاصة. وفي التجنيس؛ إذا توضأ في منزله ليصلي الظهر ثم حضر المسجد فافتتح بتلك النيَّة فإن لم يشتغل بعمل آخر يكفيه ذلك، هكذا قال محمد في الرقيات، لأن النية المتقدمة يُبقيها إلى وقت الشروع حكمًا كما في الصوم إذا لم يبدلها بغيرها. (انتهى). وعن محمد بن سلمة أنه إن كان عند الشروع؛ بحيث إنه لو سُئِلَ أية صلاة يصلي؟ يُجيب على البديهة من غير تفكر فهو نية تامة. ولو احتاج إلى التأمل لا تجوز. وفي فتح القدير: فقد شرطوا عدم ما ليس من جنس الصلاة لصحة تلك النيَّة مع تصريحهم بأنها صحيحة، مع العلم بأنه يتخلل بينها وبين الشروع المشي إلى مقام الصلاة وهو ليس من جنسها، فلا بد من كون المراد بما ليس من جنسها ما يدلّ على الأعراض، بخلاف ما لو اشتغل بكلام أو أكل أو نقول، عُدَّ المشي إليها من أفعالها غير قاطع للنية. وفي الخلاصة أجمع أصحابنا أن الأفضل أن تكون مقارنة للشروع، ولا يكون شارعًا بمتأخرة لأن ما مضى لم يقع عبادة لعدم النية، فكذا الباقي لعدم التجزيء. ونقل ابن وهبان اختلافًا بين المشايخ خارجًا عن المذهب موافقا لما نقل عن الكرخي من جواز التأخير عن التحريمة؛ فقيل إلى الثناء، وقيل إلى التعوذ، وقيل إلى الركوع، وقيل إلى الرفع والكل ضعيف والمعتمد أنه لا بد من القران حقيقة أو حكمًا. وفي الجوهرة ولا يعتبر بقول الكرخي.
Seventh: Regarding its time. The principle is that its time is the beginning of worship, but the beginning is real and legal. They said regarding prayer: if he intends before starting — according to Muhammad, if he intends at the time of wudu that he will pray Dhuhr or 'Asr with the imam, and after the intention he does not engage in something not of the genus of prayer, but when he reaches the prayer place the intention is not fresh, his prayer is valid with that intention. This is also narrated from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as in al-Khulasa. And in al-Tajnis: if he performs wudu in his home to pray Dhuhr, then goes to the mosque and starts with that intention, and does not engage in other work, it suffices. Thus said Muhammad in al-Ruqayat, because the advanced intention remains until the time of starting by legal continuity, as in fasting if he does not replace it. (End). And from Muhammad ibn Salama: if at the time of starting he would answer immediately without thought which prayer he is praying, it is a complete intention; if he needs reflection, it is not valid. And in Fath al-Qadir: they have conditioned the absence of anything not of the genus of prayer for the validity of that intention, while declaring it valid, knowing that between it and the start is the walk to the prayer place which is not of its genus. Therefore, 'what is not of its genus' must mean what indicates turning away, unlike occupying oneself with speech, eating, or we say: walking to it is considered from its acts and does not break the intention. And in al-Khulasa: all our companions agree that the best is that intention be concurrent with the start, and one should not start with a delayed intention because what passed did not occur as worship due to no intention, and similarly the remaining part due to indivisibility. Ibn Wahban transmitted a disagreement among the mashayikh outside the madhhab, agreeing with what was transmitted from al-Karkhi permitting delay after the opening takbir: it is said until the Thana', until the Ta'awwudh, until the ruku', until the raising; all are weak, and the relied-upon is that concurrence is necessary in reality or legally. And in al-Jawhara, the saying of al-Karkhi is not considered.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This is the seventh section of the chapter on intention, addressing the time of intention for acts of worship. The general principle is that the time for intention is the start of the worship, but 'start' can be real or legal. For prayer, there are multiple opinions: according to Imam Muhammad, if a person makes his intention at the time of wudu (for a specific prayer), and from that time until he begins the prayer he does not engage in anything unrelated to the prayer, then that intention suffices even if he does not recall it at the moment of starting. This is also reported from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and is the preferred view in al-Khulasa. The reasoning is that the earlier intention is legally considered to continue as long as it is not replaced. However, if he engages in speech, eating, or other actions, that breaks the continuity. Muhammad ibn Salama adds that if at the time of starting the prayer he can answer immediately which prayer he is praying, that is a complete intention; if he has to think, it is inadequate. The best view (according to our companions) is that the intention be concurrent with the start, because otherwise the past portion of the prayer would be invalid (since no intention), and it cannot be split. Ibn Wahban reports a disagreement outside the madhhab attributed to al-Karkhi who allowed delaying the intention up to various points after the takbir, but these views are all considered weak. The relied-upon (mu'tamad) position is that the intention must be concurrent with the start, either in reality or legally (i.e., not broken by unrelated actions).

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The intention in the heart which distinguishes one act of worship from another and determines its validity.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir of prayer, which marks the start of prayer.
ثناء (thana'): The supplication 'Subhanaka Allahumma' recited after the opening takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, when must the intention for prayer be made?
A) At the time of wudu
B) At any time before the prayer ends
C) Concurrent with the opening takbir, either actually or legally
D) Up to before the first sujood

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi qawida for prayer is that the intention must be made at the start, but legal concurrence allows an earlier intention to suffice if uninterrupted by unrelated acts.

intermediate

Intention Covers All Parts of Worship at Outset
Ruling on necessity of intention for every part of worship and its continuity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida that intention at the outset suffices for continuity of worship and evaluate its furuat including exceptions.

Core Idea
Intention at the beginning covers all subsequent parts of worship; renewal is not required.

When you start an act of worship, does your intention need to accompany every single action? The Hanafi school says no—once you make intention at the beginning, it flows through the entire worship unless you deliberately change it. This lesson unpacks that rule, its basis in hardship (haraj), and key applications like praying with a mistaken intention or performing tawaf with the wrong purpose.

Guided Path
1
State the Qawida
Identify the Hanafi maxim: 'Intention is not required for continuity' (لا تشترط النية في البقاء). Understand that once you intend a specific worship at the start, that intention remains valid for all its parts.
This is based on the principle of removing hardship.
2
Identify Its Scope
The rule applies to all acts of worship: prayer, fasting, hajj, etc. It covers both obligatory and supererogatory acts. The scope is any worship that consists of multiple actions or parts.
The exception is when the intention is explicitly changed.
3
Work Through the Furuat
Apply the qawida to the examples given: a) beginning an obligatory prayer but then thinking it is supererogatory – the obligatory intention carries through; b) performing tawaf with intention to seek a debtor – invalid because tawaf is an independent worship; c) standing at Arafat with same intention – valid because it is not independent.
Notice the distinction between independent and non-independent acts.
4
Identify the Istithna'
The exception to the rule is when a person intentionally substitutes a different purpose for a specific action within the worship. For example, if during prayer one intends something other than worship for a specific action, that action may be affected.
The relied-upon madhhab still holds the initial intention suffices overall.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة : هل تصح نيَّة عبادة وهو في عبادة أخرى؟ قال في القنية : نوى في صلاة مكتوبة أو نافلة الصوم، تصح نيته ولا تفسد صلاته.
الثامن : في بيان عدم اشتراطها في البقاء : للحرج وفيه حكمها في كل ركن من الأركان قالوا في الصلاة لا تشترط النية في البقاء كذا في البناية، فكذا بقية العبادات.
وفي القنية : لا يلزم نيَّة العبادة في كل جزء، إنما تلزم في جملة ما يفعله في كل حال . (انتهى).
وفي البناية : افتتح المكتوبة ثم ظن أنها تطوّع فأتمها على نية التطوع، أجزأته عن المكتوبة .
ومن الغريب ما في المجتبى ؛ ولا بدَّ من نيَّة العبادة، وهو التذلل والخضوع على أبلغ الوجوه ونيَّة الطاعة وهي فعل ما أراده الله منه، ونية القربة وهي طلب الثواب بالمشقة في فعلها وينوي أنه يفعلها مصلحة له في دينه بأن يكون أقرب إلى عقلاً عنده من الفعل وأداء الأمانة، وأبعد عما من الظلم وكفران عليه هذه النيات من أول الصلاة إلى آخرها خصوصا عند الانتقال من ركن إلى ركن. فلا بد من نيَّة العبادة في كل ركن والنفل كالفرض فيها إلا في وجه، وهو ينوي في النوافل أنها لطف في الفرائض وتسهيل لها. (انتهى).
والحاصل؛ أن المذهب المعتمد أن العبادة ذات الأفعال يكتفي بالنية في أولها ولا يحتاج إليها في كل فعل اكتفاء بانسحابها عليها إلا إذا نوى ببعض الأفعال غير ما وضع له. قالوا: لو طاف طالبًا الغريم لا يجزئه ولو وقف كذلك بعرفات أجزأه، وقدمناه. والفرق أن الطواف قربة مستقلة بخلاف الوقوف وفرَّق الزيلعي بينهما بفرق آخر وهو أن النيَّة عند الإحرام تضمنت جميع ما يفعل في الإحرام فلا يحتاج تجديد النية، والطواف يقع بعد التحلّل وفي الإحرام من وجه، فاشترط فيه أصل النية لا تعيين الجهة (انتهى). وقالوا : لو طاف بنية التطوع في أيام النحر وقع عن الفرض، ولو طاف بعد ما حلَّ النفر ونوى التطوّع أجزأه عن الصدر، كما في فتح القدير. وهو مبني على أن نيّة العبادة تنسحب على أركانها واستفيد منه أن نية التطوع في بعض الأركان لا تبطله .
Benefit: Is the intention of an act of worship valid while one is in another act of worship? It is said in al-Qunyah: If one intends in an obligatory or supererogatory prayer the fast, his intention is valid and his prayer is not invalidated. The eighth: Regarding the exposition of its non-necessity for continuity: due to hardship. And in it is its ruling in every pillar of the pillars. They said: In prayer, intention is not required for continuity, as in al-Binayah, and likewise for the rest of acts of worship. In al-Qunyah: The intention of the act of worship is not required for every part; it is only required for the entirety of what one does in each state. (End). In al-Binayah: He began an obligatory prayer, then thought it was supererogatory and completed it with the intention of supererogation; it suffices for the obligatory prayer. Among the strange things in al-Mujtaba: 'The intention of the act of worship is necessary, which is humility and submissiveness in the fullest manner, and the intention of obedience which is doing what Allah wants from him, and the intention of closeness which is seeking reward through hardship in its performance, and he intends that he does it as a benefit for his religion such that it is closer to reason according to him than the act, and fulfilling the trust, and farther from oppression and ingratitude. Then these intentions are from the beginning of the prayer to its end, especially when moving from one pillar to another. So the intention of the act of worship is necessary in every pillar, and supererogatory is like obligatory in that except in one aspect: he intends in supererogatory acts that they are a grace for the obligatory acts and an ease for them.' (End). The conclusion: The relied-upon madhhab is that an act of worship consisting of actions is sufficient with intention at its beginning and does not need it for every action, by virtue of it covering them, except if he intends by some actions something other than what it is prescribed for. They said: If one performs tawaf seeking a debtor, it does not suffice him; and if he stands at Arafat similarly, it suffices him, and we have preceded this. The difference is that tawaf is an independent act of worship unlike standing. And al-Zayla'i distinguished between them with another distinction: that intention at ihram encompasses all that is done in ihram, so renewal of intention is not needed, while tawaf occurs after tahallul and in a way within ihram, so the original intention is required, not specification of direction (End). And they said: If one performs tawaf with the intention of supererogation during the days of sacrifice, it counts for the obligatory; and if one performs tawaf after the departure has become permissible and intends supererogation, it suffices for the obligatory (sadar) as in Fath al-Qadir. And it is based on the fact that the intention of worship covers its pillars, and it is understood from it that the intention of supererogation in some pillars does not invalidate it.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage opens with a practical benefit: a person praying can validly intend an unrelated act of worship (like fasting) without spoiling the prayer. Then it moves to the eighth rule: intention is not required for continuity in acts of worship—once made at the start, it covers all subsequent parts. This is due to hardship (haraj). The author cites al-Qunyah and al-Binayah. A contrary opinion from al-Mujtaba (requiring intention in every pillar) is noted as strange, and the relied-upon position is that the initial intention suffices, unless one consciously substitutes a different purpose for a specific action. Examples: if one performs tawaf intending to seek a debtor, it is invalid because tawaf is an independent act of worship; but standing at Arafat with such an intention is valid because it is not independent. The passage concludes by reinforcing that intention at the beginning covers all pillars, and intending supererogation in some actions does not invalidate the obligatory.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The intent of the heart to perform a specific act of worship for the sake of Allah.
البقاء (al-baqa'): Continuity: the ongoing state of an act of worship after its commencement.
القربة (al-qurbah): Closeness to Allah through obedience and seeking reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi madhhab, what is the ruling if a person begins an obligatory prayer but mistakenly thinks it is supererogatory and completes it with supererogatory intention?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated.
B) It counts as the obligatory prayer.
C) It counts as a supererogatory prayer.
D) It is valid for the obligatory only if he renews intention.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule of 'no need for intention in continuity' eases worship; initial niyyah covers all parts unless a contrary intention is made.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
15 min
Intention in the Heart: Principle and Exceptions
Explains the legal maxim that intention resides in the heart, with exceptions and branch rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi legal maxim that intention resides in the heart to cases of conflict between tongue and heart, and identify the exceptions for oaths, incapacity, and judicial rulings.

Core Idea
Intention is in the heart, not on the tongue — but oaths and judicial rulings override internal intent.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir establishes a foundational maxim: the locus of intention (niyyah) is the heart, and mere verbal utterance is insufficient without it. However, this principle has crucial exceptions — oaths by Allah, incapacity to form intention, and judicial enforcement of pronouncements in divorce and manumission. The text then explores detailed branch rulings (furuat) and an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on the effect of general declarations. Understanding this maxim equips a mufti to navigate the tension between inner intent and outward expression in legal practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core maxim
The text states: 'محل النية القلب ولا يكفي التلفظ باللسان دونه' — the locus of intention is the heart, and verbal utterance alone is insufficient without it. Recognise this as a sughra (minor) maxim and a dabt (restriction) on the related maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.
Focus on the precise wording: it is not enough to simply speak the intention; the heart must be engaged.
2
Note the first principle and its exception
The first principle confirms that verbal utterance alone is insufficient. However, an immediate exception is made: if a person is unable to bring their heart to intend (due to incapacity or doubt), verbalisation suffices, based on Quran 2:286. Also, during forgetfulness, intention is not required.
This exception is governed by the maxim 'المشقة تجلب التيسير' (hardship begets facility).
3
Analyse the conflict between tongue and heart
The general rule is that the heart prevails. However, an exception is made for oaths (yamin bilah): the spoken word binds even if not intended, due to the reverence of Allah's name. For divorce and manumission, the judicial effect follows the tongue, but religiously the heart is considered.
This creates a distinction between qada (judicial) and diyana (religious) rulings — a key concept for muftis.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on general declarations
The text presents the case of a man who says 'every slave of the people of Baghdad is free' without intending his own slave. Abu Yusuf holds that his own slave is not freed; Muhammad holds he is freed. The fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view. This difference extends to divorce and other general statements.
The dispute hinges on whether general wording includes unintended individuals by default. Abu Yusuf gives weight to the speaker's intent; Muhammad gives weight to the literal generality.
5
Apply the maxim to the preacher case
A preacher, unaware his wife is present, angrily says 'I divorce you three times' to the audience. Imam al-Haramayn ruled the divorce valid, but al-Ghazali had reservations. The author analogises to the manumission case: if in a specific house, divorce occurs; if in a public place, it's subject to the ikhtilaf. This shows how the maxim is applied contextually.
The exception for oaths is also relevant: if the preacher had sworn without intent, the oath would still bind.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القنية : وإن تعمّد أن لا ينوي العبادة ببعض ما يفعله من الصلاة لا الثواب، ثم إن كان ذلك فعلاً لا تتم العبادة بدونه فسدت، وإلا فلا وقد أساء. التاسع : بيان محلها : محلها القلب في كل موضع وقدمنا حقيقتها وهنا أصلان: الأصل الأول : لا يكفي التلفظ باللسان دونه. يستحق في النية وفي القنية والمجتبى : مَن لا يقدر أن يحضر قلبه لينوي بقلبه أو يشكّ يكفيه التكلم بلسانه لا يُكَلِّفُ الله نفسا إلا وُسْعَها ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٨٦]. (انتهى). ثم قال فيها : ولا يؤاخذ بالنيَّة حال سهوه لأن ما يفعله من الصلاة فيما يسهو فمعفو عنه، وصلاته مجزئة وإن لم يستحق بها ثوابا . (اهـ). ومن فروع هذا الأصل ؛ أنه لو اختلف اللسان والقلب فالمعتبر ما في القلب. وخرج عن هذا الأصل اليمين؛ فلو سبق لسانه إلى لفظ اليمين بلا قصد انعقدت الكفارة، أو قصد الحلف على شيء فسبق لسانه إلى غيره ؛ هذا في اليمين بالله تعالى. وأما في الطلاق والعتاق فيقع قضاء لا ديانة ومن فروعه إن قصد بلفظ غير معناه الشرعي، وأما إن قصد معنى آخر كلفظ الطلاق أراد به الطلاق من وثاق لم يقبل ويدين . وفي الخانية : أنت حرّ، وقال قصدت به من عمل كذا لم يصدق قضاء. وقد حكي في شرح البسيط أن بعض الوعاظ طلب من الحاضرين شيئًا لم يعطوه، فقال متضجرًا منهم طلقتكم ثلاثا، وكانت زوجته فيهم وهو لا يعلم. فأفتى إمام الحرمين بوقوع الطلاق ثلاثا قال الغزالي وفي القلب منه شيء. قلت: يتخرج على ما في فتاوی قاضي خان من العتق قال رجل قال : عبيد أهل بلخ أحرار، أو قال: عبيد أهل بغداد أحرار، ولم ينو عبده وهو من أهل بغداد، أو قال : كل عبيد أهل بلخ، أو قال : كل عبيد أهل بغداد أحرار أو قال : كل عبد في الدنيا. قال أبو يوسف : لا يعتق عبده. وقال محمد يعتق. وعلى هذا الخلاف الطلاق وبقول أبي يوسف أخذ عصام بن يوسف وبقول محمد أخذ شداد والفتوى على قول أبي يوسف. ولو قال كل عبد في هذه السكة أو قال كل عبد في الجامع حرّ، فهو على هذا الخلاف. ولو قال كل عبد في هذه الدار حرّ، وعبده فيها، يعتق عبيده في قولهم. ولو قال ولد آدم كلهم أحرار لا تعتق عبيده في قولهم جميعا. (اهـ). فمقتضاه أن الواعظ إن كان في دار ،طلقت وإن كان في الجامع أو السكة فعلى الخلاف، والأولى تخريجها على مسألة اليمين؛ لو حلف أن لا يكلم زيدًا فسلم على جماعة هو فيهم قالوا يحنث، وإن نواهم دونه دين ديانة لا قضاء . (اهـ). فعند عدم نية الواعظ يقع الطلاق عليه فإن في مسألة اليمين لا فرق بين كونه يعلم أن زيدا فيهم أو لا . ويتفرع على هذا فروع لو قال لها يا طالق وهو اسمها ولم يقصد الطلاق لا يقع كيا حرّ وهو اسمه كما في الخانية. وفرَّق المحبوبي في التنقيح بين الطلاق فلا يقع بين العتق فيقع خلاف المشهور، ولو نجز الطلاق وقال أردت به التعليق على كذا لم يقبل قضاء ويدين ولو قال كل امرأة لي طالق، وقال أردت غير فلانة، لم يقبل كذلك. وفي الكنز : قالت تزوّجت عليَّ . فقال كل امرأة لي طالق طلقت المحلفة . وفي شرح الجامع لقاضي خان وعن أبي يوسف أنها لا تطلق وبه أخذ مشايخنا . وفي المبسوط وقول أبي يوسف أصحّ عندي، ولو قيل له ألك امرأة غير هذه؟ فقال كل امرأة لي طالق لا تطلق هذه والفرق بينها وبين مسألة الكنز مذكور في الولوالجية. وفي الكنز: كل مملوك حرّ، عتق عبيده القن وأُمهات أولاده ومدبروه . وفي شرحه للزيلعي : ولو قال أردت به الرجال دون النساء دين وكذا لو نوى غير المدبر. ولو قال نويت السود دون البيض أو عكسه لا يدين لأن الأول تخصيص العام، والثاني تخصيص الوصف، ولا عموم لغير اللفظ فلا تعمل فيه نيَّة التخصيص ولو نوى النساء دون الرجال لم يدين. وفي الكنز : إن لبست أو أكلت أو شربت ونوى معينًا لم يصدق أصلاً، ولو زاد ثوبًا أو طعاما أو شرابا دين. وفي المحيط : لو نوى جميع في لا يأكل طعاما، وجميع مياه العالم في لا يشرب شرابًا يصدق قضاء. وفي الكشف الكبير يصدق ديانة لا قضاء وقيل قضاء أيضا.
In al-Qunyah: If he deliberately does not intend worship in some of his actions in prayer, not seeking reward, then if that action is essential for the completion of the prayer, it becomes invalid; otherwise not, and he has acted wrongfully. Ninth: Explanation of its locus: Its locus is the heart in every place, and we have already presented its reality. Here there are two principles: The first principle: Verbal utterance alone is insufficient without it. Deserves in intention. In al-Qunyah and al-Mujtaba: Whoever cannot bring his heart to intend with his heart or is doubtful, his verbal speech suffices him. 'Allah does not burden a soul more than it can bear' [Quran 2:286]. (End). Then he said therein: He is not held accountable for intention during his forgetfulness, because what he does of prayer while he forgets is forgiven, and his prayer is valid even if he does not deserve reward thereby. (End). Among the branches of this principle: If the tongue and heart differ, consideration is given to what is in the heart. An exception to this principle is the oath: If his tongue precedes him to the wording of an oath without intent, the expiation becomes binding; or if he intended to swear about something but his tongue preceded to something else; this is in oaths by Allah. As for divorce and manumission, it occurs judicially, not religiously. Among its branches: If he intended a wording other than its legal meaning; but if he intended another meaning, such as the word divorce intending separation from bondage, it is not accepted judicially, and he is believed religiously. In al-Khaniyah: 'You are free', and he said 'I intended by it freedom from such work', it is not believed judicially. It has been narrated in Sharh al-Basit that a certain preacher asked the attendees for something and they did not give it to him, so he said angrily to them 'I divorce you three times', and his wife was among them while he did not know. Imam al-Haramayn gave a fatwa that the divorce occurred three times. Al-Ghazali said: There is something in my heart about it. I (the author) say: It can be derived from what is in Fatawa Qadi Khan regarding manumission: A man said: 'The slaves of the people of Balkh are free', or said: 'The slaves of the people of Baghdad are free', and he did not intend his own slave while he was from the people of Baghdad; or said: 'All slaves of the people of Balkh', or said: 'All slaves of the people of Baghdad are free', or said: 'Every slave in the world'. Abu Yusuf said: His slave is not freed. Muhammad said: He is freed. On this difference is the case of divorce. 'Isam ibn Yusuf adopted the saying of Abu Yusuf, and Shaddad adopted the saying of Muhammad. The fatwa is on the saying of Abu Yusuf. If he said: 'Every slave in this street', or said: 'Every slave in the mosque is free', then it is subject to this difference. If he said: 'Every slave in this house is free', and his slave is in it, his slaves are freed in their opinion. If he said: 'All children of Adam are free', his slaves are not freed in all of their opinions. (End). Consequently, if the preacher was in a house, the divorce occurs; if he was in the mosque or street, then it is subject to difference. The better approach is to derive it from the issue of the oath: If he swore not to speak to Zayd, then he greeted a group that included him, they said he has broken the oath; if he intended them but not him, he is believed religiously, not judicially. (End). Thus, when the preacher has no intention, divorce occurs upon him, for in the issue of the oath there is no difference between whether he knows that Zayd is among them or not. Branches branch from this: If he said to her 'O Taliq' and it is her name and he did not intend divorce, it does not occur, like 'O free' if it is his name, as in al-Khaniyah. Al-Mahbubi in al-Tanqih made a distinction between divorce (does not occur) and manumission (does occur), contrary to the well-known. If he made divorce immediate and said 'I intended to condition it on such', it is not accepted judicially, and he is believed religiously. If he said 'Every woman of mine is divorced', and said 'I intended other than so-and-so', it is not accepted likewise. In al-Kanz: She said 'I married a woman'. So he said 'Every woman of mine is divorced', the questioned woman is divorced. In Sharh al-Jami' by Qadi Khan and from Abu Yusuf that she is not divorced, and our scholars adopted it. In al-Mabsut: The saying of Abu Yusuf is sounder in my view. If one is asked 'Do you have another woman besides this one?' and he said 'Every woman of mine is divorced', this woman is not divorced. The difference between this and the case in al-Kanz is mentioned in al-Walwajiyyah. In al-Kanz: 'Every owned person is free', his own slaves, female slaves with children, and mudabbars become free. In the commentary of al-Zayla'i: If he said 'I intended by it the men without the women', he is believed religiously; likewise if he intended non-mudabbar. If he said 'I intended the black without the white' or vice versa, he is not believed religiously, because the first is a specification of the general, the second is a specification of the description, and there is no generality for non-words, so the intent of specification does not work in it. If he intended women without men, he is not believed religiously. In al-Kanz: If he said 'if I wear or eat or drink' and he intended a specific [thing], he is not believed at all; if he added 'a garment' or 'food' or 'drink', he is believed religiously. In al-Muhit: If he intended 'all' in [the oath of] not eating food, and all the waters of the world in not drinking drink, he is believed judicially. In al-Kashf al-Kabir: He is believed religiously, not judicially, and it is said judicially as well.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir presents the legal maxim that intention (niyyah) resides in the heart, not on the tongue, and then explores its applications and exceptions. The text begins with a ruling from al-Qunyah about deliberately omitting intention in prayer: if the omitted intention is for an essential action, the prayer is invalid; otherwise it is valid but the person sins. The ninth section clarifies the locus of intention: it is the heart in all matters. Two principles are given. The first principle states that verbal utterance alone is insufficient without heart intention. However, for one who cannot bring his heart to intend—due to incapacity or doubt—verbalization suffices, based on the Quranic verse (2:286). While in forgetfulness, intention is not required. Branches: when tongue and heart conflict, the heart is decisive. An exception is made for oaths: if the tongue slips on an oath, the oath is binding; for divorce and manumission, the judicial ruling follows the tongue, but religiously the person's inner intent is considered. The text then narrates a case of a preacher who unknowingly divorced his wife. The fatwa of Imam al-Haramayn held the divorce valid, but al-Ghazali had reservations. The author relates this to a manumission case: if one says a general statement like 'all slaves of Baghdad are free', Abu Yusuf says his own slave is not freed, while Muhammad says he is. The fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view, but if the declaration specifies a particular location like 'this house', the slave is freed. The preacher's case is analogous: if he was in a specific house, divorce occurs; if in a public place, it depends on the ikhtilaf. The text further discusses distinctions between divorce and manumission, the effect of adding a condition, and rulings on specifying the type of person in oaths and divorces. Finally, it covers cases of eating/drinking oaths where specification is accepted religiously and even judicially in some views.

Key Terms
النية (al-niyyah): The intention in the heart to perform an act of worship or legal act
اليمين (al-yamin): An oath sworn by Allah, with legal consequences for violation
الطلاق (al-talaq): Divorce, the dissolution of marriage

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the judicial ruling (qada) when a man says 'I divorce you' without any intention of divorce?
A) The divorce does not occur because intention is lacking.
B) The divorce occurs judicially because the spoken word suffices.
C) The divorce occurs only if the wife witnesses the statement.
D) The ruling is suspended pending an investigation of intent.

Key Takeaway
Intention resides in the heart, but in oaths, divorce, and manumission, the judicial effect follows the spoken word, creating a crucial distinction between qada and diyana.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate

Triple Talaq on a Slave Woman with 'Sunnah': Intention Overrides Phrasing
Qawida on triple talaq of a slave woman with 'sunnah' phrasing and intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida on triple talaq of a slave woman with 'sunnah' phrasing and resolve the internal dispute between al-Kanz/commentary and al-Hidayah regarding the validity of intending all three immediately.

Core Idea
The phrase 'for the sunnah' does not fix timing; the husband's intention determines the occurrence.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair presents a qawida regarding triple talaq on a slave woman (mawtu'a) when the husband adds the phrase 'for the sunnah'. The default ruling is that one divorce occurs at each purity period, but the husband's intention can alter this—whether he intends all three immediately or spaced out. Notably, there is an intra-Hanafi disagreement: the author of al-Hidayah rejects the validity of intending all three together, while al-Kanz and its commentary affirm it. As a mufti, you must understand the operative position and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qawida and its scope
First, read the core qawida from al-Kanz: 'If he says to his slave woman: you are divorced three for the sunnah, it occurs one at every purity period.' This is the default ruling. Note that it applies specifically to a mawtu'a (slave concubine).
The phrase 'li-l-sunna' here indicates the method, not a restriction on number.
2
Analyze the furu' (derived cases) based on intention
The text provides two furuat: (1) if the husband intends all three immediately (al-sa'a) or one per month, it is valid. (2) Even if he says 'for the sunnah' and intends three altogether or separately over purities, it is valid. These show that intention overrides the literal implication of the phrase.
3
Identify the internal ikhtilaf (dispute)
The commentary explicitly states: 'contrary to the author of al-Hidayah regarding intending them together.' Al-Hidayah holds that if the husband intends all three together when saying 'for the sunnah', the talaq is valid but not according to sunnah? Actually, the dispute is about validity. Al-Hidayah apparently invalidates the triple intention when the phrase 'sunnah' is used. The commentary disagrees.
The opposing view is attributed to a single author, not the entire school.
4
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The passage from al-Kanz and its commentary is the relied-upon position in later Hanafi fatwa. The husband's intention is given effect: if he intended three together, all three occur; if one per month, that too is valid. The opinion of al-Hidayah is marjuh (weak) on this point.
This reflects the Hanafi principle that in talaq, the husband's intent (niyya) is paramount.
5
Apply the qawida to a new scenario
As a mufti, you might receive a question: 'A man said to his slave woman: You are divorced three for the sunnah. He now claims he meant one per month. What is the ruling?' According to the qawida, his claim of intention is accepted (by default, unless proven otherwise), and the talaq will be one per purity period.
Intention in talaq is a matter of the husband's inner state; the qawida affirms the validity of his declared intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الكنز: ولو قال لموطوءته: أنت طالق ثلاثا للسُّنَّة، وقع عند كل طُهر طلقة، وإن نوى أن تقع الثلاث الساعة أو عند كل شهر واحدة صحت. (اهـ). وفي شرحه: أنت طالق للسُّنَّة ونوى ثلاثًا جملة أو متفرقًا على الأطهار صح، خلافًا لصاحب الهداية في نية الجملة.
In al-Kanz: If he said to his slave woman whom he has intercourse with: 'You are divorced three, according to the sunnah,' it occurs at every period of purity one divorce; and if he intended that the three occur immediately or one at every month, it is valid. In its commentary: 'You are divorced according to the sunnah' and he intended three altogether or separate over times of purity, it is valid, contrary to the author of al-Hidayah regarding intending them together.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This is a ruling from al-Kanz with commentary, discussing triple talaq on a slave woman (mawtu'a). The default: saying 'You are divorced three for the sunnah' results in one divorce per purity period. But if the husband intends something else—like all three immediately or one per month—his intention is valid. The commentary adds that even if he says 'for the sunnah' and intends three altogether or separately over purities, it's valid, disagreeing with the author of al-Hidayah who disallows intentional triple together.

Key Terms
موطوءة (mawṭūʾa): A slave woman with whom the owner has sexual relations (umm walad or concubine)
لللسنة (li-l-sunna): Divorce performed according to prophetic sunnah (i.e., one divorce per tuhr, not three together)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a man tells his slave woman 'You are divorced three for the sunnah' but intends all three to occur immediately, what is the ruling?
A) Only one divorce occurs at the first purity period
B) All three occur immediately as per his intention
C) The divorce is invalid due to violating sunnah
D) The slave woman becomes free

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when a husband pronounces triple talaq with 'sunnah' phrasing on his slave woman, his intention determines the actual effect, overriding the default of one per tuhr.

Combining Wife with Others in Talaq Utterances
Scenarios of combining wife with various entities in talaq utterances.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-jam' bayn al-mankuha wa ghayriha fi al-talaq' to determine the ruling on the wife when combined with various entities in a talaq utterance.

Core Idea
Combining wife with a non-locus in talaq can still divorce her; combining with another potential locus may void the utterance.

This passage from al-Khaniyya presents key scenarios illustrating how the presence of multiple entities in a talaq utterance affects the ruling. Understanding the concept of 'mahall li-l-talaq' (locus of divorce) is critical to predicting outcomes. We'll explore the qawida 'al-jam' bayn al-mankuha wa ghayriha fi al-talaq' and its furuat, noting the intra-Hanafi disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the entities in the utterance
List all persons or things mentioned alongside the wife: man, foreign woman (ajnabiyya), animal/stone, dead woman.
The wife is always present as one of the entities.
2
Classify each as mahall li-l-talaq or not
Only a woman in a valid marriage (or a slave woman in certain conditions) is a locus for divorce. A man, a foreign woman (unless intended as actual wife? but here she is not his wife), an animal, a stone, and a dead person are not mahall.
A foreign woman is not a mahall unless she is his wife via another marriage? But in the text, she is explicitly 'ajnabiyya' (not his wife), so not a mahall.
3
Apply the qawida: if one entity is not a mahall, the wife is divorced (with exception)
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if the non-mahall is an animal or stone (clearly incapable of divorce), the wife is divorced. However, if the non-mahall is a man (a rational being), Abu Hanifa rules that no talaq occurs because the utterance applies to both and one cannot be divorced.
Abu Yusuf disagrees on the man case and holds that the wife is divorced. Muhammad disagrees on the animal/stone case and holds that the wife is not divorced.
4
Identify the ikhtilaf in each scenario
Note where the three imams differ: man case (Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf), animal/stone case (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad), and the foreign woman case (dispute on wording and intent).
The text mentions different wordings: 'I divorced one of you' (talaq) vs. 'One of you is divorced' (without intent).
5
Determine the practical fatwa implications
The passage does not specify a mufta bihi. Later fatwa likely follows the majority or the strongest proof. Additionally, the speaker's intent (niyya) can affect the ruling in conscience (yadinu) but not in court (qada'an) in some cases.
The passage closes with a note on intent: if the speaker intended non-occurrence, he is truthful in conscience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخانية: ولو جمع بين منكوحته ورجل فقال إحداكما طالق، لا يقع الطلاق على امرأته في قول أبي حنيفة. وعن أبي يوسف أنه يقع. ولو جمع بين امرأته وأجنبية وقال طلقت إحداكما طلقت امرأته، ولو قال إحداكما طالق، ولم ينو شيئا لا تطلق امرأته وعنهما أنها تطلق. ولو جمع بين امرأته وما ليس بمحل للطلاق كالبهيمة والحجر، وقال إحداكما طالق طلقت امرأته في قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف. وقال محمد لا تطلق ولو جمع بين امرأته الحيَّة والميتة وقال إحداكما طالق لا تطلق الحية. (اهـ). ولا يخفى أنه إذا نوى عدمه فيما قلنا بالوقوع فيه أنه يدين. وفيها: لو قال لها مطلقة إن لم يكن لها زوج طلقها قبله، أو كان لها زوج لكن مات وقع الطلاق عليها، وإن كان لها زوج طلقها قبله إن لم ينو الإخبار طلقت، وإن نوى الإخبار صدق ديانة وقضاء على الصحيح، ولو نوى به الشتم دين فقط.
In al-Khaniyya: If he combined his married wife and a man and said 'One of you is divorced,' talaq does not occur on his wife according to Abu Hanifa. From Abu Yusuf that it does occur. If he combined his wife and a foreign woman and said 'I divorced one of you,' his wife is divorced. If he said 'One of you is divorced' and did not intend anything, his wife is not divorced; from both of them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that she is divorced. If he combined his wife and what is not a locus for divorce like an animal and a stone, and said 'One of you is divorced,' his wife is divorced according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said she is not divorced. If he combined his wife, a living one, and a dead one, and said 'One of you is divorced,' the living one is not divorced. It is not hidden that if he intended non-occurrence in cases where we said it occurs, he is truthful in conscience. And in it: If he said to her 'You are divorced' while she does not have a husband—if he divorced her before, or she had a husband but he died, divorce occurs. If she had a husband who divorced her before, if he did not intend informing (of the past), she is divorced; if he intended informing, he is truthful in conscience and in court according to the correct view. If he intended insult, it is only in conscience.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage from al-Khaniyya presents several scenarios of combining the wife with others in talaq utterances. First: combining wife and a man—Abu Hanifa says no talaq on wife (since 'akuma' implies both could be divorced; a man is not subject to talaq so wife is not divorced); Abu Yusuf says it does. Second: wife and foreign woman—if he says 'I divorced one of you,' wife is divorced; if he says 'one of you is divorced' without intent, wife not divorced (but from them she is). Third: wife and animal/stone—Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say wife is divorced (since the non-locus is ignored); Muhammad disagrees. Fourth: living wife and dead wife—living wife not divorced. Then a note: if he intended non-occurrence, accepted in conscience. Finally, a case: saying 'You are divorced' to a woman without a husband—if she was previously divorced or widowed, talaq occurs; if husband divorced her before, and he intended informing, accepted in court too; if intended insult, only in conscience.

Key Terms
منكوحة (mankūḥa): Married woman (wife)
أجنبية (ajnabiyya): A woman who is not married to the speaker (foreign woman)
محل للطلاق (maḥall li-l-ṭalāq): Locus for divorce: an entity upon which divorce can legally fall

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The wife is divorced.

Key Takeaway
The qawida 'al-jam' bayn al-mankuha wa ghayriha' dictates that combining the wife with a non-mahall does not prevent her divorce, except when the other entity could also be a recipient of talaq (like a man), in which case the utterance may be void.
